- **Dynamic step copy with an "already done on entry" variant must choose from the LATCHED entry state, not the live state.** `cc-clear`'s function `text` picked the "you've already deselected" line from the live `state.selected.size===0`, so it flipped to that line the instant the player cleared DURING the step — reading as if they'd done nothing. Fix: latch `tut._ccAlreadyClear` in `onEnter` and branch on it for the "already clear on arrival" variant; use the live size only to choose between the still-selected prompt and a distinct "cleared" confirmation. General rule for a function `text`: entry-conditioned messaging latches in `onEnter`; only progress-within-the-step messaging reads live state each frame.
- **A tip bubble pointed at a control that unfolds a panel should be placed PERPENDICULAR to the unfold direction — the dodge list alone isn't enough.** `ci-zoom` targeted `#l1zoomToggle` (bottom-right) with `place:'left'`; clicking it unfolds `#l1zoomCtl` leftward (the controls sit before the toggle in a right-aligned flex row), landing exactly under the bubble. `#l1zoomCtl` is already in the bubble's dodge list, but the panel only appears AFTER the bubble is placed and the placement isn't re-dodged on the unfold, so the dodge never fired. Fix: `place:'top'` (above the toggle) clears a horizontally-unfolding panel regardless of timing. Rule of thumb: anchor the bubble on the axis the panel does NOT grow along.
- **In hotseat, `state.turn` is PER-PLAYER and swaps with `setActivePlayer` — don't use it to detect that a turn was passed.** The original `cp-pass` predicate was `state.turn > (latched state.turn)`, but pressing Pass swaps the live state to player 2, whose `state.turn` is its own counter — so the comparison only went true a full round later when control returned to player 1 with an incremented counter (the step appeared to skip the first Pass and fire on the second). Fix: latch `mySeat()` in `onEnter` and advance on `mySeat() !== latched`. The active seat (`net.you` -> roster seat) is the reliable, global signal that control left the current player; the per-player game state is not. General rule: anything that must react to *control passing* keys on the active seat, not on the swapped game state.
- **Dock-pile highlight for a draw/discard step: glow the pile via `onEnter`/`onExit`, on top of the target ring.** `cp-draw` already targets `#dockLib` (so the fixed `#tutRing` frames it when the dock is open), but to make the Library unmistakable it now also toggles a `.tutpilehi` glow class on `#dockLib` in `onEnter` and removes it in `onExit` — both reliably called (`tutGo` on step change, `tutEnd` on close, each invoking the step's `onExit`). `#dockBody` has no `overflow:hidden`, so the box-shadow glow isn't clipped, and the class is added even while the dock is closed, so the pile lights up the moment the player slides the dock open.
- **The dragged-bubble pin is keyed by `tut.idx` alone, so it leaks across sections that share an index.** A pinned bubble (set when the user drags it) overrides avoidance and sits where it was parked. `intro-welcome` (idx 0) explicitly tells the user to drag the bubble, setting `_bubblePin` + `_bubblePinIdx=0`; section start (`tutStart`, ~line 12010) reset `tut.idx=-1` but not the pin, so when the next section's first step became idx 0 (e.g. `dl-open`), the stale idx-0 pin matched and the bubble appeared at the old intro-welcome position — over the highlighted element, bypassing avoidance. Fix: clear `_bubblePin`/`_bubblePinIdx` at every section start. General lesson: any per-step tutorial state keyed by `tut.idx` alone collides across sections (every section restarts at idx 0); clear it on section start (or key it by `secId+idx`).
- **Two pile element sets exist — highlight the `#z-*` board zones, not the `#dock*` peek piles, in the L4 Classic view.** `#dockCrypt`/`#dockLib`/`#dockAsh` live inside `#handPeek`; `#z-crypt`/`#z-library`/`#z-ash` are the `.zone.pile` board zones. The working crypt-draw step (`cc-draw`) targets `#z-crypt` and its ring shows; `cp-draw`/`cp-discard` were targeting `#dockLib`/`#dockAsh`, whose target ring (and a `.tutpilehi` box-shadow glow) never appeared because they aren't the visible/ringable element in that view. Fix: mirror `cc-draw` — target `#z-library`/`#z-ash` and rely on the fixed `#tutRing` (no glow needed). Lesson: when adding a dock/pile highlight, copy the element selector from a sibling step that already works rather than guessing; a box-shadow glow on the wrong (or overflow-clipped) element silently renders nothing.
- **Opening the main Menu inside a tutorial step: call `#btnMenu`'s click handler and highlight items with `menuHi`.** `onEnter:function(){ document.getElementById('btnMenu').click(); }` reuses the handler that builds the menu items (assembled inline, not a reusable fn). The handler's `e.stopPropagation()` keeps the just-opened menu from being closed by the outside-click listener. `renderItems` sets each `.mi`'s `textContent` to the item label, so `menuHi:['Leave seat']` matches exactly (tutMenuHi compares `textContent` against the labels, only while the panel is shown). `onExit:function(){ hideMenu(); }` closes it. `#menu` (z 100036) renders above `#tutLayer`, and the bubble's dodge list already includes `#menu`, so a freeInteract step's bubble stays clear of the open menu.
- **Per-seat live state that isn't in `serializeGame` is wiped on every hotseat hand-off (and lost on undo if not in `snapshot`).** `state.target` drives the play-FX red arrow (`curTargetCard`) and the log's `targetSuffix`, but was omitted from both snapshots. `setActivePlayer` hands off via `serializeGame`→`restoreGame` (which calls `clearTable`), so the target was wiped the moment control passed between seats — the feature looked broken in hotseat while being fully present in the code. Fix: add the field to both `serializeGame` and `snapshot`, and restore it guarded by `state.cards.has(id)` (the card may be gone), then repaint (`updateSelVisual()` + `updateTargetBtn()`). General rule: any live UI state that must survive a seat swap or undo has to be in the serialized blob — if a feature 'works in L1 but not hotseat', check the serialize/restore round-trip first.

- **Tripped over the documented `/tmp/original.html`-precedes-split rule myself this session — a live example of why it's a hard rule, not a suggestion.** `split_client.py`'s `SRC` is hardcoded to `/tmp/original.html` and silently ignores any CLI argument; calling it with a filename argument looks like it respects the argument (the help text implies it does) but it doesn't. I staged `/tmp/original.html` from the *pre-patch* file (habit from the very start of the session), then patched `elysium-vtes-bord.html`, then ran the split — which silently split the **stale, unpatched** copy. `node elysium-build.js` then reassembled and overwrote my patched file with the old content; `cmp` against `/tmp/original.html` "passed" because both sides were stale, masking the bug. Caught it only by grepping for the new step id in the rebuilt file and getting zero hits. Fix/discipline: `cp <patched-file> /tmp/original.html` must be the LAST thing before `split_client.py` runs, every time — re-stage it fresh after any edit, including small follow-up one-liners (e.g. a version-string bump) made after the main patch script.
- **Reaction/signal/seat-swap UI state in the tutorial is best detected by small breadcrumb flags set inline at the real call sites, not by new tutorial-engine plumbing.** Added `tut._reactClicked=true` to the `#btnDecide` click handler and `tut._lastSaidIdx=i` to `saySend(i)` (both one-liners, both harmless when no tutorial is active since `tut` is always-present). Combined with `gate:function(){...}` + `advance:{on:'manual'}` (the standard "Continue stays grey" pattern used throughout `classic-interact`/`classic-crypt`), this avoids `advance:{on:'event', ...}` + `orContinue:true`, which only offers a skip-via-Continue escape hatch rather than a genuine disabled-until-done gate — `next.disabled` is only ever set when `s.gate` exists (see `tutRender`'s `next.disabled = s.gate ? !tutGateOk(s) : false`), so an event-only step's Continue button is never actually greyed regardless of `orContinue`.
- **`qrPhasePlayed` is a single un-seat-scoped module-level `Set`, not per-player.** It's only cleared on phase change (`if(i!==state.phase){ qrPhasePlayed.clear(); ... }`), never by `setActivePlayer`/`restoreGame`. That's exactly why the Played tab can show "every card played this phase — yours and your opponents'" in one list, and it also means tutorial steps that gate on a `qrPhasePlayed.size` baseline-diff (`cx-play`, `cx-target-play`, `cx-p1-play`) work correctly across a hotseat seat swap with zero extra plumbing — the baseline is captured per-step in `onEnter`, so it doesn't matter whose plays accumulated into the set before that point.

- **`clearTable()` resetting a "show-once" flag is correct for a genuinely new game, but `restoreGame()` also calls `clearTable()` unconditionally — so every hotseat seat-swap silently re-triggers any flag reset there too.** The earlier `l4hintDone` fix ("Drag your pool globe" shows once per game) intentionally moved the reset into `clearTable()` on the assumption that `clearTable()` only ever ran for a fresh game. That assumption broke the moment `restoreGame()` (used by `setActivePlayer` for hotseat hand-off) started calling `clearTable()` as its own "wipe before repopulate" step — invisible until the new `cx-handoff`/`cx-outro` tutorial steps made a same-session round-trip seat swap actually happen in front of a user. Fix: persist `l4hintDone` in `serializeGame()`/`restoreGame()` exactly like the earlier `state.target` fix — `clearTable()` still zeroes it for a true new seat (no stored board), but `restoreGame()` overwrites it again from the blob right after, for any seat that has one. General rule (reinforcing the `state.target` lesson): **any function that is both "start fresh" and "load existing" by calling a shared reset-and-rebuild routine will leak the fresh-state defaults into the load path** unless every loaded field is explicitly re-applied after the reset — audit *all* one-shot/show-once flags the same way if more of these surface, not just this one.

- **`refreshRTargetView()` (and any other view-keyed refresh dispatcher) must enumerate every render mode, including L4 — it's easy to write the `if/else` chain against the modes that existed when the function was first written and forget the newer one.** `refreshRTargetView()` only branched on `typeof net.view==='number'` (seat visit), `'ov'` (overview), `'l2'` (columns) — `'l4'` (Classic) was missing entirely, so setting/clearing a remote target in L4 hotseat silently failed to re-paint the just-changed ring on the opponent's card (it lives in a structurally different host, `#l4oppWrap`, built by `renderL4OppCards()`/`updateL4Opponents()`, not the `#rvCards` host `refreshRTargetMarks()` knows about). The underlying data (`net.rtarget`) was fine the whole time — log text and the play-FX arrow both read it directly and weren't actually broken; the missing ring just *looked* like targeting had failed. Same family of bug as the `l4hintDone`/`clearTable` issue: a shared helper written for one set of "views"/"modes" silently drops a later-added one. **When grepping for a `net.view==='l2'`/`==='ov'`/`typeof===number` style chain elsewhere in the codebase, check whether `'l4'` (and any future view) is missing too** — this is exactly the kind of place it tends to get left out, since L4 was bolted on after L2/L3 existed.


- **Off-board UI chrome (the peek-dock) has its own, separate sizing logic from the canonical-board scale (`l2pub.s`) — don't assume one scale factor governs everything on screen.** The bottom dock (`#handPeek`/`#dockBody`: crypt/library/ash placeholders + hand cards) sits in `#tableArea` but **outside** the `l2pub`-driven board geometry entirely; its container grows correctly with the window (`height:32%`), but its CSS used the raw, static design constants (`width:var(--cw)`/`height:var(--ch)`, fixed 84×118) for the pile placeholders, and the hand cards were rendered via `qrCard(row, c, 1, 'hand')` with a hardcoded scale of `1` — neither ever read `l2pub.s` or anything else that responds to window size. Fix pattern: introduce a dedicated scale (`dockS`/`updateDockScale()`) computed from the dock's *own* `clientHeight` (minus its known CSS padding) divided by the design card height (`CH`), clamped to a sane range, written to a `:root`-level CSS custom property (`--dock-s`) per the existing CSS-stacking-context rule. CSS-sized elements (the static `.qrlib` placeholders) pick the var up automatically on resize; JS-rendered elements whose scale is baked into a `transform` at creation time (`qrCard`'s hand cards) do **not** auto-update from the CSS var alone — the render call itself has to be re-invoked (`renderHand()`) after the scale changes, e.g. from the `resize` listener when the dock is open. General rule: when a UI region grows with the window but its *contents* stay pinned at a fixed pixel size, check whether that region is actually inside the scale that "the rest of the board" uses, or whether it's a sibling region with its own independent sizing that nobody wired up.

- **Correction to the above: I patched the wrong (retired) dock at first.** `#handPeek`/`#dockBody`/`qrCard(...,'hand')` is **dead code** — `handGate()` is hardcoded `return false` with the comment "RETIRED: the visit now surfaces the REAL L2 dock", so `renderHand()`/`showHand()` always early-return and this element never shows. The REAL, live dock used in L2/L3/L4 (online and offline, any player count) is the `.l2dockopen`-driven block: the SAME `#z-crypt`/`#z-library`/`#z-ash`/`#z-hand` zone elements used elsewhere on the board, repositioned into a bottom strip via CSS (`#z-crypt,#z-library,#z-ash{width:calc(var(--cw)+34px); height:calc(var(--ch)+34px)}` etc.) and rendered by the SAME `layoutZone()`/`place()` pipeline as every other zone — but with their own scale carve-out: `place()`'s scale branch explicitly EXCLUDES piles/hand whenever `l2dockopen` is true (`s` stays `1`), per the comment "hand stays full-size when open" — so the actual live dock had the identical fixed-design-size bug, just one call-site over. **Lesson: when a UI element's purpose is described in a comment ("matches the L2 Home dock"), don't assume the element IS that thing — grep for a hard `return false`/`PARKED`/`RETIRED` gate on whatever shows/hides it before patching, especially when a sibling implementation with a near-identical name exists.** (Same family as the `l3HandHover()`-is-PARKED discovery below — this codebase has several near-twin implementations where only one is actually live.)
- **`l3HandHover()` (L3's separate "hover the hand panel to peek" overlay, independent of the full dock) is also PARKED/dead.** `function l3HandHover(on){ /* PARKED: the L3 hand lives in the shared dock now... */ }` — a no-op. `l3handOpen` is therefore never set `true` by any live caller, so every `!l3handOpen` condition in `place()`/`layoutZone()`/elsewhere is unconditionally true in current play. Confirmed before relying on it (rather than assuming) — worth re-checking if it ever gets un-parked, since several scale/visibility branches are written `(l2dockopen || l3handOpen)` and currently only the first half is reachable.
- **A per-card scale baked into a fixed-size UI region requires updating THREE layers in lockstep, not just the resting-state CSS: the box size, the resting-state per-card render scale, AND any drag/gesture math that assumes a specific old scale.** Fixing the dock's fixed-size bug touched: (1) CSS `calc()` geometry for the zone boxes + pool glob + log panel (additive `* var(--dock-s)` factors), (2) `place()`/`layoutZone()`'s pile/hand centering math (a `forceS` param added to `place()` so the dock branch doesn't have to fight the existing `l2pub.s` branch), and (3) `regrabAtScale()` + the L4 `drag.l4DockDefer` transition logic, which both **hardcoded the assumption that the dock's resting scale was exactly `1`** (`Rx=drag.ox-CW/2` with no normalization; `sc=1` when `l4DockDefer`; `regrabAtScale(c,drag,1)` on dock-entry). Missing layer (3) wouldn't show up in the client-logic test suite (pixel/gesture math isn't unit-tested) or even in a static read of the rendering code — it would only surface live, as a card jumping to the wrong size or position mid-drag the moment it crossed the dock boundary. General rule: before changing a "renders at scale 1" constant anywhere, grep for every place that constant is *assumed* downstream (drag-transition math, regrab/recenter helpers, anything computing an offset "as if full size"), not just where it's read for normal rendering.

- **Regression from the dock-scaling fix: scaling factor was computed against the wrong dimension.** First cut of `updateDockScale()` did `dockS = (boardHeight*0.32 - 36) / CH` — i.e. "fit the available strip height with the CARD height (118px)." But the thing being scaled is the zone BOX (`CW|CH + 34px` = 152px tall, card + padding), not the bare card. So on a laptop (board ~650px) it produced dockS≈1.46, making the box 222px tall inside a ~208px (32%-of-board) strip → boxes hung out past the dock top, and the log's left edge (anchored after the now-wider piles, fixed right edge) got pushed ~127px right and squeezed. **Fix: scale proportionally to board height, calibrated so dockS=1 at the canonical 616px board height (where the original fixed-size dock was designed to fit):** `dockS = clamp(boardHeight/616, 0.6, 1.8)`. Because the 152px box already sat well inside the strip at 616px, `H/616` keeps that same fraction at any height — grows on bigger windows, provably never overflows (box-top stays below strip-top for all H under this formula). **General lesson: when deriving a scale factor "to fill" a container, the numerator and denominator must be the SAME dimension of the SAME element** — don't divide the container's height by the inner card's height when what scales is the larger padded box; and prefer calibrating a scale to a known-good reference size (dockS=1 ↔ 616px) over an absolute "fill this many px" computation, which is far easier to get subtly wrong.
- **All of L2/L3/L4 set `l2cols` on `#board`** (confirmed: `renderL2`/`renderL3`/`renderL4`/the L4 setup all add it), and `#board.l2mode.l2cols` is `position:absolute; inset:0; transform:none !important` — so in every one of these views `#board` fills `#tableArea` with NO CSS transform. Consequence: the dock zones (children of `#board`, sized in px) are NOT auto-scaled by any board transform; their on-screen size is literal px, so a dedicated scale (dockS / `--dock-s`) is the only thing that grows them with the window. (The `#board.l3mode{ /* ...fitBoard() scales it... */ }` CSS rule on its own line is an EMPTY comment-only rule and is stale/misleading — L3 gets its sizing from `.l2cols`, not from a 1004×616 fitBoard transform. Don't trust that comment.)

- **The dock backing (`#l2dockbg`) height is best tied to the zone geometry, not a fixed percentage, once the zones scale.** With the dock content scaling linearly (dockS = H/616) but the backing fixed at `height:32%` of the board, the gap between the top of the zones and the top of the dark gradient was a constant ~5.8% of board height (≈ 0.32 − [1.5% bottom offset + scaled box height as a fraction]) — so the "air" at the top grew with the window. Fix: set the backing height to `calc(1.5% + (var(--ch) + 34px) * var(--dock-s) + 14px)` — the zone's own bottom offset + the same scaled box height the zones use + 14px clearance (9px for the `.zcount` count badge, which overhangs the box top by 9px and is NOT scaled by --dock-s, + ~5px margin). This hugs the boxes identically at every window size and dockS value. Note the badge overhang (`.zcount{top:-9px}`) is a FIXED 9px regardless of dockS (the badge isn't scaled), so the clearance term is a constant px, not a scaled one. Both `#l2dockbg` rules need it (the `l2mode:not(.l3mode)` one for pure L2, and the `l3mode` one — which also covers L4 since L4 carries `.l3mode`).
- **Reducing the dock backing height does NOT require touching the hover-to-close hysteresis, but it does loosen it slightly — a tradeoff worth surfacing rather than silently "fixing".** The close threshold is `yd < H*0.66` (cursor above 34%-from-bottom closes the open dock), repeated across ~6 sites (the pile/hand put-back cancel zones at ~3922/4022, the hover open/close at 3943-44/4046-47/9381-82/9389-90, and the L4 drag-defer at 8684). The original 32% dock top sat at 0.68-from-top, just 0.02 below the 0.66 threshold (a 2% forgiving band). The new hugging height puts the dock top at ~0.71-0.72-from-top, so the same 0.66 threshold now leaves a ~5% band above the visual dock where the cursor is off the dock but it hasn't closed yet. Not broken — arguably nicer (more forgiving) — but if exact original feel is wanted, the threshold would need to track the new dock-top fraction (which now depends on dockS, so it'd have to move into JS and thread through all ~6 sites). That's a delicate-system change (drag/hysteresis has a history of interlocking bugs), so it should be a deliberate, separately-verified step on request, not folded into a cosmetic height tweak.

- **The `l4`-missing-from-a-view-dispatch pattern recurred in FOUR places, not one — it's worth auditing every such chain whenever a new render mode is added.** After the Target one (`refreshRTargetView`), Johan found two more (roster-sync, the player-colour setting) and the audit turned up a fourth (hotseat give). All share the shape "a dispatch written against `number`/`ov`/`l2` (the modes that existed when it was written) that silently drops `l4` (Classic, added later)." The four: (1) `roster(m)` handler — needs `renderL4()` (FULL rebuild, since a roster change alters the globe SET; `updateL4Opponents()` only updates existing globes); (2) `applyPco()` (player-colour setting) — needs `updateL4Opponents()`; (3) `refreshRTargetMarks()` — see the #rvCards-scope note below; (4) `giveHot()`'s post-give re-render — needs `updateL4Opponents()`, reachable in L4 hotseat via `qrGiveToTarget` (play-from-hand onto a set target). Cleared as NOT bugs after checking: `turn(m)` (only `ov` — correct, because L4 has no per-board turn indicator; only L3 mats show a ▶, and the global `#phases` bar is handled unconditionally by `updatePhaseGlow()`); the rtarget-clear sites at 6778/6820 (teardown/join, view switches anyway) and 7120 (followed by a full re-render in the same handler). **Audit rule: grep `net.view==='l2'`/`==='ov'`/`typeof===number` chains AND `l4on()`/`l3on()` board-class chains whenever adding or touching a render mode; the `net.view`-keyed ones are where `l4` gets dropped, while the `l4on()`/`l3on()`-keyed ones (e.g. 5720/5737) tend to be correct because they were written board-class-first.**
- **`refreshRTargetMarks()` queried only `#rvCards`, but the remote-card HOST differs per view** — `#rvCards` for a seat visit (`renderRemote`), `#l3stage` for L3/overview (`renderL3`), `.l2pane2` panes for L2 columns (`renderL2`), `#l4oppWrap` for Classic (`renderL4OppCards`). All four are `board.appendChild`-ed (or an overlay), and the `.rc` cards in them all carry `data-cid` + `data-seat` (set by `addRCard` from `ctx`). The `#rvCards`-only query meant the lightweight Target-ring toggle silently no-op'd in L2 and L3 (their cards aren't in `#rvCards`), so clicking an opponent card to set/clear a target updated the button + log but NOT the on-card ring until a full re-render — invisible bug online (periodic opponent board-updates re-render and mask it), but **persistent offline/hotseat** (no such updates). Fix: scope the query to `document.querySelectorAll('.card.rc[data-cid]')` (host-agnostic; L4 is handled separately by `refreshRTargetView` routing to `updateL4Opponents`, so it's never ring-toggled here). The function's own stale comment said it covered "seat / oval / L2" — "oval" was the PARKED pre-L3 overview that *did* use `#rvCards`; the comment was never updated when ov→`#l3stage` and L2→panes. Lesson: a refresh that scans a specific container DOM is fragile when the thing it scans for can be hosted in different containers per mode — prefer a class/attribute selector scoped as widely as the elements can appear, or the scan silently misses the modes whose host moved.

- **`net.rtarget` (cross-board target) had to be added to `serializeGame`/`restoreGame` to be per-seat in hotseat — `state.target` was already there, but the two targets live in different places and only one was being persisted.** `state.target` (targeting your OWN minion) is a `state.*` field, saved at serialize 8217 / restored 8256. `net.rtarget` (targeting ANOTHER seat's card — what the tutorial's Target lesson uses) is a `net.*` GLOBAL and was persisted nowhere, so a hotseat priority hand-off (`setActivePlayer` → `serializeGame`/`restoreGame`) left the outgoing player's `net.rtarget` live on the incoming one. Symptom wasn't just a stuck lit Target button: with a stale `net.rtarget` pointing at the now-active player's own seat, their next hand-play hit `if(net.rtarget){ qrGiveToTarget(c) }` (8030) instead of `playFromHand`, routing into `giveHot(ownSeat,…)` which injects the card into their own stored board — state corruption from a normal play. Fix: save `rtarget:net.rtarget||null` and restore `net.rtarget = (d.rtarget && d.rtarget.seat!=null) ? d.rtarget : null`, parallel to `state.target`. NOT validated against `state.cards` (it points at another seat's `net.boards[seat].pub`, not the local board) — the existing snapshot/roster pruning (7118-7121 / 7141-7144) nulls it if the target card is gone. Additive JSON field, so older clients ignore it (no wire-protocol break; the blob isn't even sent over the wire in normal online play). Lesson: when persisting "the current target" for a seat hand-off, remember there are TWO targets (local `state.target` and cross-board `net.rtarget`) in different namespaces — persisting only the `state.*` one silently leaks the global across hand-offs.
- **`targetersOf()`'s `if(!inRoom())` guard was unnecessarily online-only — the hotseat infra already has everything it needs.** Hotseat sets `net.roster` (with names), `net.you` (the active player, updated every priority switch at 7604), and `net.boards[seat].pub.target` (because `buildPub` stores the cross-board target at 8307 WITHOUT an inRoom gate). So the same "⌖ who is targeting this card" tags work offline by relaxing the guard to `if(!inRoom() && !localTable)`. Lower-impact than the rtarget fix (the active player sees their own target as a RING, not a tag, and is skipped via `p.name===net.you`), but it removes an online/offline asymmetry that matters once you have 3+ hotseat seats cross-targeting. Worth checking, when you see an `if(!inRoom())` early-return in a rendering/derive helper, whether the data it needs actually exists in hotseat too (`localTable`) — several of these guards predate the hotseat feature and are stricter than necessary.

- **Archiving the "dead" legacy hand dock (#handTab/#handPeek/#dockBody) was NOT a clean lift — dead and live code were physically interleaved, and the safe move was a no-op stub + leaving guarded refs, not a wholesale delete.** Three traps: (1) the hand-card type-sort helpers (`HAND_TYPE_ORDER`/`handTypeWords`/`handTypeTuple`/`handTupleCmp`/`handSortCmp`) sit *inside* the dock's code region but are LIVE (used by `state.zones.hand.sort` at ~8164 and deck grouping at ~5126/5137) — they had to stay in place; (2) `renderHand()` is called from live refresh paths (`renderAltIfOpen`/`switchView`/the move handler), so it became a documented **no-op stub**, not a deletion — deleting it would have thrown at 6 call sites; (3) `updateDockScale()` lives in the same region but is LIVE (drives `--dock-s` for the real `.l2dockopen` dock, called from `layout()`). Every reference to the removed fns/elements was already `typeof X==='function'`- or `if(el)`-guarded (the original author wrote those guards defensively precisely so the dock could be removed), so the removal was safe; the `'dockCrypt'`/`'dockLib'` array entries in the pile-flash/drag wiring were trimmed (consistent with how `avLib`/`qrLib` were trimmed earlier). **Method that worked: an atomic Python patch (`assert s.count(old)==1` per edit, write only after all asserts pass) for the ~9 interleaved edits, then sanity-grep that dead defs are gone (count 0), live helpers remain (count 1), and live callers are intact — before the syntax/test/byte-roundtrip gates.** Lesson: "this whole block is dead" is rarely true for code that grew organically — grep each symbol's call sites first; a function can be a no-op in effect (early-returns) yet still be load-bearing as a call target, and utility helpers often get physically parked next to the feature that first needed them while being used elsewhere.

- **`avRank` sort in `renderPlayed()` was inherited from the retired Reaction Window and caused Played-tab instability.** The sort (`isAction?2:actSt==='played'?1:0`) grouped cards by action-status, but `actSt` on rank-1 cards ('played') is mutated to 'resolved' by `resolvePlayedActions()` when a new action starts or the phase advances. This dropped the card from rank 1 to rank 0 mid-turn, visibly jumping it toward the bottom of the overlay with no user action. Fix: `collectPlayed()` reverses the iteration over `state.zones.ready` and `pub.cards` (both are zone-insertion-ordered old→new, so reversing gives newest-first) and `renderPlayed()` removes the sort. The display order is now stable and chronological — cards only leave the list when they leave the ready zone. Lesson: before keeping any sort from a retired UI surface, verify whether the sort key is stable during normal play; `actSt` is a mutable runtime field and was actively being mutated by normal play actions.

- **`+/−` keyboard shortcuts can be made context-aware by checking `state.selected` before deciding what to bump.** The pattern `const c=singleSelectedCounter(); c?bumpCounter(c,±1,'blood'):bumpPool(±1)` reads cleanly and mirrors how ctrl/shift+click already dispatches to the card under the pointer. The `pushUndo()` call in the keydown handler runs before `a.fn()`, and `bumpCounter`/`bumpPool` each call `pushUndo()` internally on the first call of a "run" — but `pushUndo()` deduplicates against the last snapshot, so the double call is safe (nothing has changed yet when the internal one fires).

- **When a sort order is "wrong for one use-case but right for another", make it a `conv.*` toggle instead of hard-coding a winner.** The `avRank` sort in `renderPlayed()` was wrong for a stable chronological view but genuinely useful for live-action grouping. Adding `conv.playedSort` ('new'/'action') with a `<select>` in Settings lets the user decide. The conditional sort is four lines; the wiring (conv default + load + openSettings init + change handler + renderAltIfOpen call) is the bulk of the change. Pattern for future display toggles: add to conv object → load block → Settings HTML → openSettings() init → change handler → immediate re-render.

- **`box-shadow` is the right choice for a secondary visual indicator on an element that already uses `outline` for another purpose.** `#playedRow .avc.avsel` uses `outline:2px solid #dcb872; outline-offset:3px` for the selection ring. The batch highlight (`avc-batch`) uses `box-shadow:0 0 0 2px ... 0 0 9px 2px ...` — a spread-only inner ring + outer glow. Both can be active simultaneously on the same element without one clobbering the other (CSS only allows one `outline` but arbitrary `box-shadow`). The `border-radius` must be repeated on both rules since each sets it independently.

- **Adding an optional boolean parameter to a shared lambda is cleaner than duplicating it or branching outside.** The `act(verb,fxv)` helper was used by six menu items including Block. Adding `resolve=true` as a third default parameter meant the five true actions needed zero changes; only Block explicitly passes `false`. The call to `resolvePlayedActions()` is placed BEFORE auto-lock + log so the overlay re-render (triggered inside `resolvePlayedActions → renderAltIfOpen`) sees the final resolved `actSt` state at the same moment the log entry appears.

- **A shared global counter (`_avSeq`) stamped onto cards at play time (not stored in `state.zones` order) is the right way to get cross-seat chronological ordering.** Zone arrays are insertion-ordered per-seat, not globally. `_avSeq` is incremented in `tagPlayed()` and preserved through ALL round-trip paths (snapshot/restoreSnap for undo, serializeGame/restoreGame for autosave + hotseat hand-off, buildPub for opponent pub). The restore pattern `c._avSeq=sc._avSeq||0; if((sc._avSeq||0)>_avSeq) _avSeq=sc._avSeq` ensures the counter is always advanced past restored values so new plays never collide with old ones.
- **Dynamic help overlay sections: use a hidden div + show/hide in the open handler, not static HTML.** The `setHelp(on)` closure (inside the helpToggle IIFE) was extended to call `updateActionFlowHelp()` when `on` is true. This keeps the logic close to the open event and avoids a separate scroll/open event listener. The hidden div `#helpActionFlow` is always in the DOM but only shown when `conv.playedSort==='action'`.

- **A per-client incrementing counter is NOT globally orderable online — use a `Date.now()` timestamp when you need cross-client chronological order with no coordination.** `_avSeq` (Played-tab play order) started as `++_avSeq` per client. In hotseat that is shared via serialize/restore, so it is monotonic across seats; but ONLINE each client's counter starts at 0 independently, so merging seats in `collectPlayed()` interleaved them by incomparable numbers. Switching to `c._avSeq=Date.now()` makes the value globally comparable across independent clients for free. Bonus: a timestamp is only ever COMPARED, never "advanced past a restored max" — so the `if((sc._avSeq||0)>_avSeq) _avSeq=sc._avSeq` advance logic in the restore paths could be deleted. Add a deterministic tiebreaker (card id `'c'+mintOrder`) for same-millisecond collisions. **General rule: if a sort key has to be comparable across machines that never talk to each other, a wall-clock timestamp + a stable id tiebreaker beats any locally-minted sequence number.**
- **When a new sortable field is added to cards, audit ALL the paths that reconstruct a card, not just serialize/restore + buildPub.** `_avSeq` was added to `snapshot`/`restoreSnap` (undo), `serializeGame`/`restoreGame` (autosave + hotseat), and `buildPub` (opponent pub) — but `restoreFromPub()` (host restoring an online player's saved-snapshot board) was a fourth reconstruction path that initially missed it, so those cards would all have sorted as 0. The four card-reconstruction paths in this codebase are: `restoreSnap` (undo), `restoreGame` (load/hotseat), `restoreFromPub` (online host snapshot-restore), and the live `makeCard` minting. A new per-card field that needs to persist generally has to be wired through all of them.

---

## Cross-board card lifecycle learnings (v2.5.20–2.5.26)

- **Snapshot-based undo cannot reverse a cross-board move.** `snapshot()` captures only your own `state.cards`; `restoreSnap` does `state.cards.get(id)`. So a card `destroyLocal` removes at give-time is unrecreatable by any snapshot, and another seat's board is unreachable. Cross-board give / take-back therefore push a **semantic undo entry** (the same pattern as the `UNDO_DRAW` sentinel) that reverses itself. `undo()` dispatches these via `applyUndoEntry(s)` — objects on the stack are distinguishable from snapshot strings and the `UNDO_DRAW` string, and `pushUndo`'s `===` dedup between a string and an object is safely false, so a heterogeneous stack is fine.
- **`destroyLocal(c, opts)` gained a `keepUndo` flag** (mirroring `move()`), so a cross-board move can suppress the stack-wipe and push its own entry instead. Any operation that removes a card but wants undo preserved must pass it.
- **`makeCard(name, kind, fid)` takes an optional id.** This is the whole basis of online recall: the **giver generates a `gid` and sends it**, and the recipient's `given` handler passes it as `fid`, so both sides reference the same card. Without a shared id the giver can't name the card to recall it. (Collision risk of `'g'+Date.now()+random` is negligible but real — a monotonic counter would remove it.)
- **A recall's destination is owner-side, so Burn is a free variant of recall.** The holder only *removes* the card and confirms; the owner remembers whether it goes to hand or ash (in `net.recalling[cid]`) and spawns it accordingly on `recalled`. That is why "Burn to my ash" needed no server or holder change — only the owner-side spawn differs. `net.recalling` is also the guard that stops a stray `recalled` from spawning a duplicate.
- **In-place edits on a card you control but don't hold use one generic `ctrl` message.** The server routes it (owner → holder, adding `from`); the holder validates `owner === from` and applies it to its **live** card with the normal functions (`c.blood`, `renderCounters`, `schedulePush`). Hotseat has no holder, so it mutates the board JSON (`net.hot.boards[seat]`) *and* the public snapshot (`net.boards[seat].pub`) and re-renders. The action set is a switch — new actions (lock/flip/counters) are one branch each on both sides.
- **`buildPub` already exports `owner`, `controller`, and `blood` per card.** This is what makes the online controller menu possible: the holder broadcasts `owner`, so the giver sees their card with `owner === net.you` and the menu appears; and `ctrl` blood changes propagate because blood is in the public view.
- **Opponent-card interactivity is gated by `if(ctx)` in `addRCard`.** The `rc` class, `data-cid`, `data-seat`, and the click/contextmenu handlers (including the controller menu) are only attached when `ctx` is present. So the *board* renderers (`renderRemote` = visit, `renderL3` = overview/mats, `renderL4OppCards` = Classic) get interactive cards, while flat/peek renders (Ready-peek minions, Played tab) get inert display cards — and `opponentSurfaceAt` only ever finds the interactive ones. Any new opponent-card interaction rides this gate.
- **There are two give drag-systems; both funnel through `giveTo`.** bindCard's pointerup + geometric `opponentSurfaceAt` covers L2/L3/L4 (its L4 branch scans `#l4oppWrap`); `startGiveDrag` (bound on the visit hand strip, active when `net.view` is a number) covers a single-board visit with its own `elementFromPoint` hit-test. Write a give behaviour once in `giveTo`/`giveHot` and both paths — and both transports — inherit it.
- **Double-click plays, drag gives.** The "double-click gives when a target is set" branch lives in `qrTap`, reachable only via `qrCard('hand')`, which is never called (the live hand is rendered by `layoutZone` → bindCard → `tap()`, which just plays). So a set target shows in the log/animation but never attaches the card; attaching is a drag onto the minion.

## v2.5.27 learnings (dock peek-log fix + robust tutorial gates)

- **`--dock-s` is height-derived, but width is what constrains the dock.** `updateDockScale()` sets `--dock-s = clamp(boardHeight/616, …)`. So do **not** scale the dock's whole horizontal extent by `dock-s`: the hand (fixed 440px) and the pool offset are deliberately kept in **fixed px**; only the three piles scale (modestly) and the log fills the rest. Scale everything horizontally and the dock overflows on an ordinary 16:9 big screen (dock-s up to ~1.8 × the px offsets > screen width). At `dock-s=1` (the canonical 616px height) every `*dock-s` expression must be a no-op against the old constant — otherwise you're changing the laptop look, not just the big-screen drift.
- **A zone whose *width* scales but whose *gap* to its neighbour is fixed will eventually overlap.** `#z-pool` had `width:130px*dock-s` but a fixed 138px to the log → overlap once `dock-s > 1.06`. Fix: make the neighbour's offset track the scaled width (`+ 130px*dock-s + 8px`), not a fixed sum.
- **`max-width:calc(Npx * var(--dock-s))` + a retained `right:Npx` tames an edge-anchored panel proportionally** without touching the laptop look: on small screens the natural width sits below the cap (unchanged), on large screens the balloon is clipped. The constant is a tuning value and is **not** covered by the logic suite — it needs live verification.
- **Robust tutorial gate = poll a monotonic signal that only the target action moves.** For "press Undo", `hand.length >= base` is wrong (a draw also grows the hand). `undoStack` only *shrinks* on Undo while every other undoable action *grows* it, so `undoStack.length < base` (measured in the step's `onEnter`, after the card is played) detects exactly an Undo. General rule: find the counter/stack that moves in the *right direction only* for the action you're waiting on, rather than a visible side-effect several actions share. (`playFromHand` itself doesn't `pushUndo()`, but the gesture/menu paths do it before the play — otherwise a played card couldn't be undone at all and the button wouldn't enable.)

## v2.5.28 learnings (tutorial: menu auto-open pitfall + leaving without saving)

- **Don't open a menu inside a tutorial step and expect the next click to land on a highlighted item.** The global outside-click listener (a document `pointerdown` that calls `hideMenu()`) closes the menu on the *very first* click anywhere outside it — including the tutorial's own Finish button. So an `onEnter` that does `btnMenu.click()` + `menuHi:['…']` looks right but the menu vanishes on the first interaction. Instead: ring the button (`target:()=>$('#btnMenu')`) and *describe* the item in the step text. (v2.5.28: `cx-leave`.)
- **Leaving the tutorial game without saving it:** the tutorial game is mirrored only to `TUT_GAME_KEY` (via `tutGamePersist()`, gated on `tutGameLive`), kept apart from the regular autosave (`saveKey()`). `leaveHotseat()` writes `TUT_GAME_KEY` one last time when `tutGameLive`. To leave *without* saving: set `tutGameLive=false` **before** calling `leaveHotseat()` (skips its save branch), then `removeItem(TUT_GAME_KEY)` + the per-chapter snapshots (`tutClassicKeys().forEach(tutChapKey)`, matching the Reset path). The regular autosave needs no special handling — `leaveHotseat()` runs `clearTable()`, so the next flush removes `saveKey()` (empty board).
- **A capturing keydown handler that opens a modal needs a re-entry guard.** `tut.esc` is registered with capture (`true`) so it beats the global Esc handler; once it `await`s a `uiConfirm`, a second Esc while the dialog is open re-enters the same async function. Guard with a flag (`tut._ending`, cleared in `finally`). Note the capturing handler also swallows Esc while the confirm is open (Esc won't cancel it — the Cancel button does); acceptable.

## v2.5.29 learnings (Shift-to-peek vs Shift+click)

- **A bare-modifier keydown that shows an interactive overlay clashes with click-gestures using that same modifier.** Shift-to-peek (`#logPeek` on Shift keydown, active only when the side panel is collapsed) collided with **Shift+click to adjust the token under the pointer** (blood / pool) on the board: the peek panel popped up the instant Shift went down, and because `#logPeek.peeking` sets `pointer-events:auto` (so its card links are hoverable) it could even swallow the click. Fix: neuter the keydown activation (mechanism kept dormant). Rule of thumb: don't bind a plain `Shift`/`Ctrl` keydown to a UI action in a view where the same modifier is also part of a click gesture — the keydown fires the moment the user presses the modifier *for the click*.

## v2.5.30 learnings (undo hover, auto-captured undo labels, major.minor lockstep)

- **An inline `style.translate` silently overrides a CSS `translate`-property lift.** Card positioning uses `style.transform`; the hand hover-lift uses the *separate* CSS `translate` property (`.card.handhover{ translate:0 -26px }`). Drag-start sets an inline `el.style.translate='none'` (to snap a frozen residual) and nothing cleared it — so any dragged-then-in-hand card (undo is one path) kept the inline `translate:none`, which **beats the stylesheet**, and never floated on hover. Fix: clear `el.style.translate=''` in `place()`. General rule: `transform` and the individual `translate`/`rotate`/`scale` properties are independent; if you set one inline for a gesture, clear it when the gesture ends, or a class-based rule on the *other* property looks like it “stopped working” on exactly the elements you touched.

- **Auto-capturing an undo label from the action’s own log line avoids labelling every caller.** To make Undo say *what* it reversed without threading a label through ~20 `pushUndo` call-sites: wrap snapshot entries as `{s,label}`, have `pushUndo` arm `_undoCap=entry` and drop it after the sync tick (`Promise.resolve().then(...)`), and have the top of `log()` grab the first string message into `_undoCap.label`. Every action logs its own description right after `pushUndo`, so the label captures for free; actions that don’t log (or are async across the tick) fall back to a bare “Undo.” Gotcha: the shared undo stack is heterogeneous (snapshot entries + `UNDO_DRAW` sentinel + give-objects), so `applyUndoEntry` must key “is this semantic?” on a **discriminator** (`s.t`), not merely `typeof s==='object'` — otherwise a wrapped `{s,label}` snapshot is mistaken for a semantic entry and consumed as a no-op instead of restored. Verified first that every non-snapshot push already carried `.t`, and that the stack is never persisted, before changing the entry shape.

- **Relaxing the server `vWarn` to `verMM` ends the restart-on-every-client-patch tax.** Under strict lockstep (v2.5.26–2.5.29) the server’s exact-match `vWarn` warned the moment a client-only patch bump shipped, forcing a redeploy just to silence a cosmetic message. Making the server compare major.minor (`verMM(m.v)!==verMM(VERSION)`), mirroring the client, means a client-only patch (2.5.x → 2.5.x+1) is silent on both sides and needs no restart, while a genuine major/minor drift still warns. Caveat: the release that *relaxes* `vWarn` is itself a server change, so it needs a final restart.

## v2.5.31 learnings (Clan/Path auto-detect: printed KRCG path never fed the detectors)

- **A menu-gating check and a detection function can silently drift apart when a new data source appears.** `_krcgPath` (the printed Path field KRCG started shipping after PR #830) was wired to *hide* the "Follow Path…" menu for vampires with a fixed path, but was never written into `c.path` — the only field `detectPath()`, `pathCount()`, `clanChoiceItems()`'s path list, and the on-card path badge actually read. Result: printed-path vampires were correctly recognised for the menu-gate but invisible everywhere else, because the "gate" and the "detectors" were two different consumers of the same logical value and only one of them was updated. **Fix:** `krcgPath(c)`/`effPath(c)` helpers (same non-mutating, computed-from-`cardInfo` pattern as `detectClan()`) — `effPath(c) = c.path || krcgPath(c)` — used everywhere "the path this vampire follows" is needed, keeping the printed/permanent vs. chosen/undo-able state cleanly separated (never write `krcgPath` into `c.path`). **General rule:** when a new data source starts feeding "the same logical field" your code already tracks, grep every reader of that field — not just the one the bug report points at — since a partially-wired source looks correct in the one place someone tested it.

## v2.5.33 learnings (dock Hand/Log proportional split)

- **A "scale some siblings, fix others, let one fill the remainder" layout guarantees the filler absorbs 100% of any growth.** The dock's Hand box was fixed px while Log filled the leftover space up to a `dockS`-scaled cap; both piles and Pool DID scale with `--dock-s`. Result: as the window grew, all the extra room landed on Log alone (Hand never moved), breaking the laptop-calibrated Hand:Log proportion — even though nothing was individually "broken," each rule was locally reasonable. When siblings should hold a visual ratio under scaling, give them **the same scale factor**, not "some scale, one absorbs the rest."
- **Clamp proportional siblings together, against a REAL measured bound, not a proxy.** `--dock-s` is height-only (`H/616`); a screen wide instead of tall could grow it past what the board's actual width can host. Scaling Hand+Log by `dockS` alone (the naive fix) reintroduces v2.5.27's overflow bug. Fix: compute both at `dockS`'s rate, then if their combined width exceeds the board's *actually measured* remaining width (`board.clientWidth` minus the other elements' real offsets), scale both down by the same factor — ratio preserved, overflow impossible, and it's a no-op at the laptop-calibrated size where the pair already fit.
- **New JS-computed dock sizes go on `:root` as custom properties, mirroring `--dock-s` itself** (`--dock-hand-w`/`--dock-log-w`), not a class rule — `position:absolute` descendants across stacking contexts don't reliably see vars set via class rules (documented for `--dock-s`, holds for its siblings too).
- **Setting an explicit `width` on an absolutely-positioned element that also has `left`+`right` set is safe and simply overrides `right`** (per the CSS spec, `right` is ignored once `left`+`width` are both specified) — used to replace `#dockLog`'s old `max-width` cap with an exact JS-computed `width`, without needing to also touch its `right:10px` declaration.

## v2.5.34 learnings (End Tutorial wiped per-chapter snapshots)

- **When a new mechanism is built on top of an existing cleanup routine, the cleanup must be updated to respect the new data.** `tutCancel`'s cleanup (v2.5.28: "drop everything so nothing resumes") predated the per-chapter entry snapshots (added later as replay checkpoints). The cleanup was never narrowed to match, so it destroyed exactly the data the newer mechanism depended on. General principle: any time you add a new persistence layer, grep every existing cleanup/reset/clear path and decide whether the new data should survive each one.
- **Simulate the ACTUAL exit path, not an approximation.** The first probe used `tutEnd()` + `leaveHotseat()` (the two things `tutCancel` does *among other things*), which gave a false green. `tutCancel` inserts a destructive `localStorage.removeItem` loop between those two calls — the exact line the probe bypassed. Testing a simplified approximation of a function is not the same as testing the function itself; call the real thing.


## v2.5.39 learnings (touch batch T0+T1)

- **Synthetic-event bridging reaches frozen inline handlers - the old "touch requires handler-body extraction first" claim is superseded.** The 18 inline `contextmenu` listeners and the pile-drags' `pointercancel` cleanups are all reachable by *dispatching real events at them* (`new MouseEvent('contextmenu',{bubbles,cancelable,clientX,clientY})`, `new PointerEvent('pointercancel',{bubbles:true})`): the long-press engine synthesises what the platform withholds on touch and every existing handler runs unchanged, capture-phase ones included. The full extraction remains a worthwhile *testability* refactor, but it is no longer a prerequisite for the touch roadmap (this supersedes the Fas-3 note further up this file).
- **`touch-action` evaluation stops at the nearest scroll container - an ancestor's `none` does NOT block a descendant scroller.** The chain consulted for a pan runs from the touched element up to and *including* the first scrolling element; anything above it (here `#board{touch-action:none}`) is never asked. So `#dockLogList` keeps native finger-scroll under the board's `none`, the planned pointer-scroll shim was unnecessary (shelved), and per-element `none` is only needed where an element can render *outside* the locked ancestor (`.card` - remote cards live in `#rview`). `touch-action:pan-y` on in-board scrollers is kept purely as declared intent.
- **A synthetic `pointercancel` event does NOT fire `lostpointercapture`** - that event is generated by the UA when capture is actually released, not by an element receiving a cancel. Consequence for gesture teardown: capture-based gestures whose cleanup lives in a `lostpointercapture` listener (`bindCard`/`bindTokenDrag`) must be torn down by **directly nulling their module-global** (safe pre-threshold: nothing has `.moved`, so their pointerups no-op), while gestures with a **document-level `pointercancel` listener** (`libDrag`/`cryptDrag`) ARE reachable by dispatching the event (it bubbles to the document; their cleanups release capture + listeners properly).
- **`-webkit-touch-callout:none` on `body` also kills the iOS *paste* callout inside text fields** (it inherits) - long-press in the room-password input would silently lose Paste. Pair the body rule with an explicit restore: `input,textarea{ -webkit-user-select:text; user-select:text; -webkit-touch-callout:default; }` (the global `user-select:none` had the same latent effect on selection).
- **CSS `transform:scale()` enlarges the hit box, not just the pixels** (hit-testing respects transforms) - scaling the hover-hidden pool +/- buttons *in place* (`translateY(-50%) scale(1.3)`) grows both visual and tap target without touching any `left/right` offset math, sidestepping the layout-collision risk of changing `width/height` on absolutely-positioned siblings.
- **Window/document-level gesture listeners must be pointerId-scoped or a second finger warps them.** The marquee's `window pointermove/up` and the felt-pan's document listeners consumed *every* pointer's events; on multi-touch the second finger stretched the box / fed the pan. Stamp the owning `pid` at gesture start and filter every move/up/cancel on it - and give such gestures a `pointercancel` mirror of their `pointerup` (real cancels happen on touch: browser takeover, incoming calls; the long-press engine also relies on it).


## v2.5.40 learnings (touch batch T2 - steppers)

- **A hold-to-repeat driving an `async` action needs a modal guard in the tick.** `bumpCounter` can `await uiConfirm` (the influence-limit helper); a finger still holding the button would stack one confirm per 90 ms tick. The repeat loop checks `#overlay.show` and stops itself - the generic rule: before wiring a repeat/interval onto ANY existing action, read the action for `await`/modal paths first, and make the loop yield to them.
- **Replace, don't wrap, when converting click-driven buttons to pointer-driven repeat.** `bindHold` fires on `pointerdown`; if the element kept its old `click` handler too, every press would double-fire (down-step + native click-step). The pool +/- conversion swapped the four click bindings and the L4 globe's delegated click out entirely - grep for existing `click` handlers on a control before adding any pointerdown behaviour to it.
- **Route element-specific taps through the existing gesture pipeline instead of intercepting in capture phase.** The badge-tap -> stepper path stamps `drag.badgeKind` in `bindCard`'s own pointerdown and resolves in `tap()` - zero new capture listeners, no propagation fights with the drag arm or the long-press engine, mouse behaviour untouched by construction, and (crucially) `tap()` can return BEFORE the `lastTap` double-tap arm so a badge tap never half-arms a lock/flip. Pattern: when a sub-region of an already-bound element needs its own tap meaning, carry a discriminator on the gesture object.
- **Every new hold/repeat control must join the long-press engine's skip-list.** Holding a repeat button IS a long press; without the exemption the engine fires at 450 ms, the global fallback opens the quick-phrase menu mid-repeat, and the click-swallow eats the next tap. The skip-list (`#ctStepper,.ctstep,.pbtn,.l4pbtn` + the T1 set) is now a checklist item for any future press-and-hold control.
- **A menu-embedded control needs an item type that skips the leaf bindings.** `renderItems` closes the menu on every leaf click; the stepper row uses a new `{el}` item type that just appends the element - no close, no `pushUndo` wrapper (the control manages its own) - so the menu stays open while the player steps blood up and down.

## v2.5.41 learnings (touch batch T3 - pinch/pan/dock)

- **A multi-pointer gesture owns its pointers via capture-phase `stopPropagation`.** Once the pinch activates, its document-capture move/up/cancel handlers stopPropagation for the two tracked pointerIds - every element-level and document-BUBBLE listener (globe drags, hover trackers, the lupp) simply never sees those events. This is far cleaner than per-gesture teardown for closure-local state (the globe's `gd`) that no global can reach: don't chase every consumer, own the events. Capture-at-document + stopPropagation blocks same-pointer bubble listeners but leaves other pointers untouched.
- **Teardown routing recap, now with three tiers (extends the v2.5.39 learning):** module-global capture-based gestures -> direct-null with their cancel-cleanup bodies; document-listener drags with unconditional cleanups (`libDrag`/`cryptDrag`) -> one dispatched `pointercancel` reaches them; **pid-scoped document mirrors (the felt-pan) -> the dispatched `pointercancel` must carry the RIGHT `pointerId`** (`new PointerEvent('pointercancel',{pointerId:id,...})` per tracked finger), or the mirror's own filter drops it.
- **Two handlers on the same element can hand a gesture off through a module global + registration order.** The marquee handler (registered first) creates `mq` when the one-shot arm is set; the pan handler (registered later, same pointerdown) sees `if(mq) return` and yields. No flags passed, no coupling beyond the shared global - but the semantics DEPEND on listener registration order, so the dependency is stated in comments at both sites.
- **Anchor a floating affordance to the element whose geometry it must track, as a child.** The dock-close chip lives INSIDE `#l2dockbg` at `top:-15px`: the backing's height is a `--dock-s` calc that changes with every window size, and a body-level chip would need the same formula duplicated in JS. As a child it rides the edge for free.
- **On precision touchpads, pinch arrives as `ctrlKey` wheel events with fine-grained deltas** - a fixed per-event zoom step (x1.12) feels notchy there while staying right for mouse wheels. Branch on `e.ctrlKey`: proportional `Math.exp(-deltaY*k)` for the pinch stream, the discrete step for plain wheel. (`preventDefault` on the wheel handler is what stops the browser's own page-zoom for ctrl-wheel - it was already there.)
- **"Pan closes it" is usually better implemented as "touch-down on the surface closes it".** The felt-pan starts at pointerdown with no threshold, so gating the dock-close on "a pan" versus "a touch" is the same code path - and closing on a mere tap outside is the standard mobile dismissal pattern (a strict superset of the planned behaviour, recorded as a deliberate deviation in the plan).

## v2.5.42 learnings (touch batch T4+T5 - roadmap complete)

- **When a touch path performs an action a native listener might also synthesize, give the touch path a yield window instead of trying to predict the browser.** Whether a `click` follows a preventDefaulted touch `pointerdown` varies by engine; `_tapDrawAt` (touch draw stamps it, the four native click/dblclick listeners return for 500 ms) makes double-draw impossible on EVERY engine without needing to know which one fired what.
- **A touch double-tap helper needs two guards, not one:** (1) a long hold must never arm half a double-tap (`>350 ms` press = long-press territory - without this, lifting off a long-press then tapping again would fire the double action), and (2) on Android the browser ALSO synthesizes a native `dblclick` for a double-tap, so a fired helper arms a one-shot document-capture suppressor (`_dtAte`) that eats the duplicate. iOS fires nothing - which is why the helper exists at all.
- **Compatibility mouse events after touch make hover-tooltips sticky.** A tap on an element without a preventDefaulted pointerdown synthesizes `mouseover` at the tap point - the tooltip shows and there is no `mouseout` until the next tap somewhere else. Track the last pointerType on the (already-running) document pointermove and have the mouseover listener stand down after touch input; cheaper and more precise than `(hover:none)` media checks on hybrid devices.
- **An inline-transform-positioned element gets its coarse sizing by folding the factor into the SAME placement math - and the anchor constant tells you how.** The Edge button's L3 placement centres via `fx+fw/2-16` (half its 32 px) with a `0 0`-origin `scale(Z)`; multiplying the scale by `_ek` alone would drift the centre by `16*(k-1)*Z`, but writing `-16*_ek` in the offset keeps the CENTRE fixed while the button grows. Read the hardcoded half-size in the anchor math before scaling anything positioned this way (the same family as the v2.5.27 dock-scale lesson: find every place the old size is ASSUMED).
- **A privacy rule expressed as an absent attribute gates features for free.** Face-down cards deliberately carry no `data-card-name` (v1.6); the Inspect row simply hides when `c.faceDown` and `pinHover` no-ops without the attribute - the feature cannot leak what the attribute never exposes. Prefer building new inspect/preview paths ON the attribute rather than re-deriving visibility rules.

## v2.5.43 learnings (the desktop-regression audit)

- **Replace-not-wrap has a keyboard blind spot: converting `click` handlers to `pointerdown` silently drops Enter/Space activation.** Keyboard activation of a `<button>` fires a `click` with `detail===0` and NO pointer events. The clean restoration inside the pointer helper: `el.addEventListener('click', e=>{ if(e.detail===0) fn(); })` - pointer-driven clicks carry `detail>0`, so nothing double-fires. Checklist line for every future click->pointer conversion.
- **`navigator.maxTouchPoints` lies on some Windows driver stacks** (phantom >0 with no touchscreen), so it must never flip a UI mode alone - pair it with `matchMedia('(any-pointer:coarse)')` (a REAL coarse pointer exists) and keep a manual override. `pointer:coarse` alone is also insufficient the other way (touchscreen laptops report a fine primary pointer), which is why the pair is needed.
- **Any proportional-from-deltaY wheel math needs `deltaMode` normalization or Firefox breaks quietly** (line mode, deltaY around +/-3 vs Chrome's ~100 pixels) - the discrete sign-only branch never noticed, the new exponential branch was near-inert there. Normalize (x16 per line, x viewport per page) BEFORE feeding deltas into any formula.
- **Audit method that worked:** classify every edit as (1) touch-only property/media (inert for mouse by spec), (2) `pointerType`/`touchUI` gated branch (verify the else-path is line-identical), (3) guard that must be logically unreachable with a single mouse (argue it: capture discipline + target exclusions), or (4) genuine shared-path change - then grep-verify only class 4 and anything the old code's `stopPropagation` might have been protecting. Three class-4 findings out of ~80 edits, all hardened same-session.

## v2.5.44 learnings (the L3 pentagon width constraint)

- **An interlocking layout's clearance must be an EXPLICIT constraint, not an emergent property.** The pentagon deliberately lets the mid band Y-overlap the bottom band (that's how five boards fit), which makes horizontal clearance the ONLY collision guard - yet the width formula never encoded "three abreast". It held on wide felts by luck (the laptop's margin: **6.5 px**) and failed below felt-AR ~1.89. When a layout relies on rects interlocking, write the separation condition INTO the size solver (`wlim3=(aw-2mX-gx)/3`) and prove the reference case unchanged (Bw 357.015 -> 357.015).
- **Slice-and-run beats read-and-reason for geometry bugs.** Cutting the LIVE `l3geom`/`l3slots` out of the file (brace-counting extraction, zero transcription) into a Node harness with programmatic rect-intersection checks found in minutes what arithmetic-with-guessed-constants kept getting wrong - and produced the before/after evidence table for free. The harness also verifies the FIX in situ against the patched file. Reusable for any slot-math question.
- **A user's pinpoint observation is a binary-search probe.** "Prey and predator overlap MY board, the others are fine" eliminated the mats, the timer, the grid and 2-band branches in one stroke and aimed the AR sweep at exactly the mid-vs-bottom pair. Ask WHICH elements before hypothesizing WHY.
- **Fallback branches that approximate the normal path drift into being a separate (buggy) mode.** `!l3canonAR -> raw-AR full-bleed` produced precisely the low-AR felts that defeated the implicit clearance. Self-heal the state with the SAME formula the normal path uses (`l3canonAR=(W+asideComp)/H` in place) instead of maintaining a parallel geometry - one behavior, zero fallback class, and both callers (l3slots + the L4 geometry) heal identically.
- **"Perfect on my machine" can mean "6 pixels from the cliff".** The reference configuration sitting barely inside a constraint is a smell worth checking whenever a layout works at one size and fails at another - compute the actual margin, don't trust the screenshot.

## v2.5.45 learnings (uniform L3 scaling)

- **"Everything just visually bigger" is a testable theorem, not a vibe: assert `layout(s*window)/s == layout(reference)`.** The similarity harness (constant AR, scale sweep, per-coordinate compare) turns the user's expectation into a 0.085 px pass/fail — and instantly exposes every absolute px term as a violation source. Any future layout claiming scale-invariance gets this assert.
- **Converting px constants to fractions needs a CALIBRATION reference, stated in the code.** Each term is written as `value/reference_dim` at a named felt (1095x534) so the old tuned look is reproduced to float precision (0.003 px) at that size and pure similarity holds elsewhere. Never invent "nice" fractions — derive them, and comment the division so the next tuner knows where the number came from.
- **`max(floor, fraction)` clamps are hidden non-uniformity when the floor binds at the reference.** cb/clockW's floors (36/90) exceeded their fractions at laptop size, so the layout silently ran on the floor there and on the fraction on big screens - a drift source with zero px-addend in sight. Recalibrate so floor==fraction AT the reference: above it the fraction rules (uniform), the floor only guards smaller windows.
- **Pure proportionalization can beat a base-scale (k-clamp) rearchitecture.** Same user-visible result, but zero transform-chain surgery: clampL3Pan, the zoom-about math, l2pub's Z-invariant and the shared L4 stage all stay untouched, and the diff is eight self-evident line edits inside one solver. Prefer making the MATH scale-free over adding a scaling LAYER, when the function is pure enough to allow it.
- **Residual differences between physically different screens are the L2-equivalent contract, not a bug.** After proportionalization the only remaining variance is the screens' true content-area AR (canonAR 2.051 vs 1.990 - the +244 aside term reconstructs full width; the monitors simply differ), moving the 5p gap 6.5->9 px because a different constraint binds. Same-screen enlargement is exact; cross-screen follows AR exactly like L2 does. State the residual to the user instead of chasing it silently.

## v2.5.46 learnings (the undo coverage audit)

- **Audit undo the same way you audit transport: diff MUTATIONS against CAPTURE, programmatically.** Grep every `c.X=`/`state.X=` in the codebase, parse the field list out of `snapshot()`, cross-reference `serializeGame` (a field in the save blob but not the undo snapshot is either a doctrine decision or a bug - `state.target` was the founding example, `masterBonus`/`turn`/`edgeTok` were this round's). Manual cleanup needed: spread captures (`counters:[...c.counters]`) and push/splice-mutated arrays are invisible to the naive regexes on BOTH sides.
- **`log()` is load-bearing infrastructure, not cosmetics.** Non-private log lines call `scheduleSave()` -> `schedulePush()`, which is the ONLY reason a snapshot-undo propagates to online opponents and marks the autosave dirty. Removing or privatizing an action's log line silently breaks its sync. Any new state-mutating path must either log or call scheduleSave explicitly.
- **When a flag and its numeric effect are set together, capture both.** `trifleUsed` (captured) and `masterBonus` (not) were written by the same action - undo restored the flag but left the +1, a phantom the HUD happily displayed. Snapshot review checklist: for every captured boolean, ask what NUMBERS the same action touched.
- **A restore function that mirrors another restore function must mirror ALL of it.** `restoreGame` synced the free Edge token (ensure/remove + position); `restoreSnap` only restored the holder boolean and repainted the chip - the felt token ghosted. When two restores share state, diff their bodies, not just their field lists.
- **Self-healing consumers lower severity but don't excuse asymmetric capture.** `undoCryptDraw`/`undoDiscard` skip entries whose cards moved - so the uncaptured histories were "mostly fine" - but capturing them (like `drawHistory` already was) makes the semantics exact instead of approximate. JSON.stringify in `snapshot()` deep-copies for free, so history entries never alias live state.
- **Document the declined scope with the decision-maker.** Token DRAGS remain non-undoable by Johan's explicit choice ("not necessary") - recorded here so a future session doesn't "fix" it as an oversight. The position IS captured, so undoing PAST a token move restores the then-current spot; only the move itself lacks its own undo step.

## v2.5.47 learnings (L3 chrome relocation)

- **A mode-gating check is not exclusive just because it reads like one.** `l3on()` returns true during L4 too — entering L4 adds BOTH `l2mode`+`l3mode`+`l4mode` to `board.classList`, so any code branching on `if(l3on())` (like `setCenterFrameA`'s Edge-positioning branch) silently runs during L4 as well. Before gating shared code on a mode check, grep where every relevant class gets added/removed — don't infer exclusivity from the function name.
- **A new module-global flag driving a HIDE must default to the pre-change behaviour, and only the ONE function with new knowledge may flip it.** `l3centerOnFelt` defaults `true` (today's behaviour everywhere) and only `renderL3()` sets it `false` (only place that knows N). Any OTHER render path that shares the gated code (here: `renderL4()`) needs an explicit defensive reset at its own top, even if analysis suggests it "should" already be fine — staleness from a previous render is a real risk once a flag is shared across two independently-invoked functions.
- **Persistent DOM elements need explicit hide-reset on mode exit; elements the mode already destroys don't.** `#l3timer` is created fresh every L3/L4 render and removed wholesale by `clearL3()` - its `.hidden` state can never leak. `#edge`/`#edgeChrome`/`#statsL3Info` are static top-level elements that persist across the WHOLE session - `clearL3()` needed three explicit new reset lines or an N!=5 session's hidden Edge marker would stay hidden forever, even back in L1/L2.
- **Gate the OUTER shell of an existing code block, not its internals, when the internals are calibrated/delicate.** The Edge felt-positioning code (T5's `_ek` coarse-factor math) went untouched inside a new `if(eg && l3centerOnFelt){ ...unchanged... }` wrapper, rather than threading the new condition through the existing lines. Preserves "N=5 is byte-for-byte identical" as a structural guarantee, not just a tested outcome.
- **A hardcoded `target:()=>$('#selector')` in tutorial/coachmark code is a hidden dependency on that element always being visible.** Search coachmark/onboarding arrays for every element a change might hide - the 2-player tutorial (one of the NOW-relocated player counts) had a step pointing straight at `#edge`; the fix is a one-line fallback (`el.hidden ? fallback : el`), cheap insurance once you know to look.
- **When relocating a HUD element into an existing options panel, insert as a sibling OUTSIDE the panel's own full-rewrite region.** `renderStats()` replaces `#statsBody`'s entire `innerHTML` every call; `#statsL3Info` lives between `#statsHead` and `#roomBar` instead, with its own dedicated update function - never fighting the rewrite, never needing to be re-inserted after every stats refresh.

## v2.5.48 learnings (the aside-transition race)

- **A synchronous flag update + a CSS width transition = two clocks; never mix a post-toggle flag with a pre-transition measurement.** `setAside()` flips `asideCollapsed` instantly while the panel animates over 140 ms - reading `clientWidth` on the next line pairs the OLD width with the NEW flag, and any formula compensating via the flag (the +244 term) silently inverts its own correction. The fix costs nothing: **measure BEFORE the toggle**, when width and flag are a consistent snapshot - the compensation formula then works in both prior states by construction.
- **Sticky capture vs live derivation decides whether a transition race is a bug or a cosmetic blink.** The same race hits every setAside site, but only where the mismeasured value is CAPTURED into persistent state (`l3canonAR`) - with its recapture deliberately guard-blocked - does it become a lasting layout fault. Sites that re-derive geometry from live dimensions each render (L2 columns, fitBoard) self-heal via the existing rAF+200 ms settle resizes. When auditing a race class, classify each site by "captured or derived?" first; it collapses the fix list fast.
- **`dispatchEvent` runs handlers synchronously - a flag cleared on the line AFTER a dispatch is still SET during the handlers.** `setAside`'s settle mechanism dispatches its synthetic resizes before `_asideResize=false`, so the resize handler's canonAR-recapture is blocked even at the 200 ms "settled" dispatch. Here that is INTENTIONAL doctrine (aside toggles must never reflow the felt - the +244 compensation owns that case), and it is now documented as such so nobody "fixes" the ordering and breaks the doctrine. But the pattern is worth recognising: dispatch-then-clear means "handlers see the guard up", clear-then-dispatch means "handlers see it down" - choose deliberately.
- **"Toggling away and back fixes it" is a fingerprint for enter-path state capture racing a transition.** The second entry measures an already-settled layout. When a user reports that exact recovery gesture, go straight to the enter function's synchronous sequence and look for a measurement downstream of an animated toggle.
- **A comment asserting ordering ("X must run first") deserves a why - and gets inverted wholesale when the ordering flips.** The old comment said `setAside() above must run first so asideCollapsed is current` - locally true, globally wrong (currency of the flag was the PROBLEM). The replacement explains the race, the persistence mechanism, and why pre-toggle is correct in both prior states.

## v2.5.49 learnings (the [hidden] CSS footgun)

- **Any element with its own explicit `display` CSS property (via id/class) silently defeats the `hidden` attribute unless reinforced.** A browser's `[hidden]{display:none}` default is an ordinary-priority rule; ANY author rule that also sets `display` on the same element (regardless of how "normal" it looks, e.g. `#foo{display:flex}`) wins over it. This is a well-documented, commonly-hit HTML/CSS gotcha (MDN calls it out explicitly). The codebase already had FOUR precedent fixes for it (`#helpOverlay[hidden]`, `.tok[hidden]`, `.set-row[hidden]`, `#hoverCard .htok[hidden]`) before this session - the pattern was known, just not checked against when v2.5.47 introduced NEW `.hidden` toggling on elements that already had their own `display` rule.
- **New checklist item for any future `el.hidden=...` toggle: does the element's own CSS set `display`? If yes, add `#id[hidden]{display:none}` in the same patch, or the JS logic will be correct and silently do nothing visually.** Grep `\[hidden\]{` before shipping any new hide/show feature to confirm the reinforcement is present for every newly-hidden-toggled element.
- **A user's precise, oddly-specific-sounding request ("remove the button now") can be a signal that a previous fix didn't actually take effect - take it as a prompt to re-verify your own recent work, not just implement the literal ask.** The JS logic (`eg.hidden=!l3centerOnFelt`) was exactly correct; only the CSS reinforcement was missing. Re-reading one's own recent diff against known codebase gotchas (rather than assuming "I already fixed this") caught it.
- **When fixing a footgun, grep for siblings sharing the same exposure and consider including them defensively even without a confirmed report** - `#l3resetBtn` has the identical risk profile (pre-existing, unrelated to this feature) and was folded into the same reinforcement rule while the pattern was fresh in mind.

## v2.5.50 learnings (reordering a shared-budget flex row)

- **A width-sharing formula (`avail = total - fixed_stuff`) is order-independent by the commutativity of addition — reordering the ROW doesn't require touching the MATH, only the position formulas.** `updateDockScale()`'s `leading`/`trailing` split was written assuming Hand-then-Log's specific adjacency, but the actual computed NUMBER (total space for the two flexible elements combined) is identical regardless of where those fixed elements physically sit in the row. Recognizing "is this quantity a sum of fixed widths, or does it depend on adjacency/position?" before touching code saves a much bigger rewrite.
- **When two elements share a flexible budget, moving one AWAY from the other doesn't break the split — it just means the shared budget occupies two separate row-gaps instead of one contiguous one.** CSS doesn't care that Hand and Log are no longer adjacent; each just needs its own correct `left` + the SAME computed `width` custom property. The visual "shared budget" relationship survives being physically split apart.
- **Reordering N absolute-positioned siblings sharing one coordinate baseline is a single shared-prefix insertion, not N independent recomputations.** Every downstream formula already expressed its position as `baseline + relative-offset`; giving the new first element the OLD baseline and prepending `newElementWidth + gap` to every other formula preserves all their EXISTING relative offsets unchanged - five near-identical one-line edits instead of re-deriving five new formulas from scratch.
- **A numeric proof harness (compute both old and new arrangements, assert identical total + no overlap) is cheap insurance for a "just reorder it" request that turns out to touch a shared-budget system.** Three representative sizes (calibration point, max clamp, min clamp with active overflow-squeeze) caught nothing here, but would have caught a sign error or missing term immediately, and produces the same before/after evidence table that geometry work in this project has repeatedly relied on.
- **When the person offers a follow-on idea "but let's see how this feels first," record the idea in project-context under On the horizon and stop there.** Scope discipline: ship exactly what was asked, park the rest visibly rather than half-implementing it or dropping it silently.
