Adding a new "try this first" tier to `imgUrl()`'s ~18 call sites looked like it would require touching every site (to teach each one about the new tier and its OWN failure case) — a large, error-prone diff across code with genuinely different existing behaviours per site (some retry webp→jpg, some swap in `BACKS.*`, some hide the element and reveal a text fallback). The fix needed zero of those sites touched: a single `document`-level `error` listener registered with `capture:true` fires BEFORE the target element's own listener gets a turn (capture always precedes target/bubble in DOM dispatch), so it can recognise "this failure was MY new tier" specifically, `stopPropagation()`, and hand off to the next tier — and if that also fails, the interceptor's own pattern-match naturally stops applying, letting the ORIGINAL per-element handler run exactly as it always did. General shape: to prepend a tier in front of a heterogeneous existing fallback chain, intercept and rewrite via a single ancestor-level capture listener rather than modifying every leaf.

## v2.6.2 learning: `norm()`'s alphanumeric-only output is what makes it possible to reuse as a filename-safety guarantee, not just a display-normalisation step

The server's `/images/` route needed to accept exactly the filenames the client would ever request, while rejecting path traversal outright. Because `norm(name)` already strips everything except `[a-z0-9]` (for card-name matching purposes, unrelated to file safety), the SAME regex that validates "is this a real norm()'d name" also, for free, makes `/` and `..` unrepresentable in a matching string — a validation rule reused from an unrelated part of the codebase turned out to double as the security guarantee, rather than needing a bespoke sanitiser.

## v2.6.3 learning: a per-ELEMENT retry guard (dataset flag) is not the same thing as a per-CARD memory across renders — asking "does this scale?" out loud is what surfaced it

`el.dataset.localImgTried` (v2.6.2) correctly stopped a SINGLE `<img>` element from looping on its own fallback, but a card rendered many times across a session gets a FRESH element each time (drawn, played, hover-previewed, re-laid-out), so the per-element guard offered zero memory between those renders — a subtly different scope than it looked like at a glance. Johan's plain question ("is this checked once at startup, or every time") was the thing that made this visible; the fix (a small session-scoped `Set` the shared `imgUrl()` checks first) is the standard shape for "remember a negative result across many independent call sites" and generalises: per-element/per-call guards prevent a LOCAL loop, not a repeated GLOBAL cost, and the two are easy to conflate when a fallback pattern is written to solve the local case first.

## v2.6.4 learning: "what covers this asset" is worth a full inventory pass before designing the fix, not just extending the first mechanism found

The initial ask (v2.6.2) was scoped to card art via `imgUrl()`. When Johan asked to extend coverage to backs and icons, a full grep for every hardcoded `static.krcg.org` reference surfaced THREE different existing patterns (a plain-property pair, two CSS url() rules, and three independently-duplicated svg functions) — each needing a DIFFERENT fix shape (getters; JS-set-at-use-time; a shared extracted helper). Designing against only the first one found would have missed two of the three. The inventory grep (`grep -n "static.krcg.org"` across the whole file) took under a minute and changed the shape of the entire fix.

## v2.6.4 learning: verify a new regex dispatch against concrete examples BEFORE trusting it in the running app

Before wiring the widened error-listener regex into the actual page, a five-line standalone Node script ran the exact same regex + dispatch logic against six representative URLs (a card, both backs, two svg shapes, an unrelated URL) and printed the classification for each. This caught nothing this time, but it is the cheap, fast way to validate "does my regex correctly separate these lookalike cases" independent of DOM/browser behavior, before relying on the harder-to-inspect live error-event path to prove it.

## v2.6.5 learning: after several incremental patches to the same feature, re-read it as ONE continuous block before calling it done

v2.6.2 through v2.6.4 each made locally-correct, individually-verified changes, but each patch was reasoned about (and placed) relative to the code AROUND its own insertion point, not relative to the OTHER patches from earlier turns. Reading the whole assembled result as a single, uninterrupted stretch (rather than re-deriving it from memory of "what I changed") surfaced a forward-reference (BACKS defined before the consts its getters read) and a duplicated tail (svgUrl's cache-or-network logic, copy-pasted rather than called, into the error listener) — neither visible from any single patch's diff in isolation, both obvious once read start-to-finish as one thing. Worth doing this kind of consolidated re-read after any feature that grew across 3+ separate patches, even when every individual patch was gated green.

## v2.6.6 learning: read your own verification printouts as EVIDENCE, not as ceremony

The v2.6.5 dispatch re-verification printed `unrelated.png -> CARD:unrelated` — the extension-permissiveness bug, sitting in plain sight in my own output — and I read it as "re-verification passed, same results" because the line I was LOOKING FOR (the reorganisation preserving behaviour) was fine. A verification run answers exactly the question you ask it; unexpected lines in its output are free additional findings, but only if actually read. Corollary: when a printout includes a case you didn't design the current change around, that case deserves one conscious beat of attention before moving on.

## v2.6.6 learning: replacing a declarative preload (CSS url) with lazy JS loading silently drops the preload — and a top-level browser API needs a typeof-guard under the Node harness

Two halves of the same fix. (1) CSS `background:url(...)` doesn't just SET an image — it also causes the browser to FETCH it at parse time. Moving that image to JS-at-use-time (v2.6.4, for the local-folder toggle) kept the setting but silently lost the fetching, so the first-ever drag could show a blank ghost on a cold cache. When removing a declarative resource reference for runtime flexibility, ask what ELSE the declaration was doing for free (preloading, here) and restore it explicitly. (2) The restored preload used `new Image()` at top level — which threw `Image is not defined` under the Node test harness (it stubs document/$ but had never needed an Image constructor). Browser-only constructors used at top level in a file that ALSO runs under the harness need a `typeof X!=='undefined'` feature-detect; the alternative (stubbing Image in the harness) would silently mask the same class of issue for the NEXT browser-only API too.

## v2.6.7 learning: external news ("there's a zip") doesn't just simplify a plan — it can invalidate an implementation ASSUMPTION the plan was quietly compensating for

The planned download-images.js would have taken a --fmt flag matching conv.imgFmt, silently guaranteeing folder-format == setting-format. The zip removes that guarantee: the player no longer chooses the format, KRCG does. So the right response to "acquisition is easier than we thought" was not just to cancel the script but to hunt for what the script WOULD have been keeping consistent — and make the consuming side robust to its absence (the format-agnostic ladder). When a plan dies, list its side-effects before burying it.

## v2.6.7 learning: negative memory (missing) sometimes needs a positive twin (wrong-format) to avoid re-paying a discovery cost per render

localImgMissing alone couldn't express "the file EXISTS, just under the other extension" — without a second Set, every render of a jpg-on-disk/webp-configured card would re-walk the miss→retry ladder, the exact per-render tax v2.6.3 eliminated for the missing case. The pair (localImgWrongFmt routes imgUrl straight to the extension that exists; localImgMissing routes straight to the network) partitions the outcome space so each card pays the discovery walk exactly once per session, whatever the outcome. Pattern: when adding a fallback LADDER, give each rung that can succeed its own memory, not just the final failure.

## Pre-release learning: `tail -3` on a gate's output is self-inflicted blindness — the gate spoke, I muted it

check-versions had been printing the lockstep warning and the stale protocol header for MANY turns; my own gate invocations truncated its output to the last three lines every single time, so the warnings never reached the transcript. The v2.6.6 lesson ("read your own printouts as evidence") has a prerequisite this pass exposed: the printout must be ALLOWED to reach you first. Gates exist to talk; truncate their output only after consciously deciding which lines are safe to lose — or better, run the full output at least once per session and always before a release.

## Pre-release learning: a "cosmetic" version-string drift can be a live user-facing bug — check what actually READS the string

The client-2.6/server-2.5 lockstep break looked like pure bookkeeping until grepping for what consumes the version: `verMM()` compares major.minor on EVERY join and sys-messages '⚠ Version mismatch — Update the older one.' to the player. Every public user would have seen a false warning on day one. Before classifying any constant drift as cosmetic, find its readers.

## v2.6.8 learning: persist user INTENT at the moment of the click, not at the completion of the work it starts

conv.cardDB was set on line one of its button's handler; conv.imgCache waited for a multi-minute download to finish cleanly. The second pattern has a failure window exactly as long as the work: any reload/close in it strands the durable side-effects (a full IndexedDB) behind an unset flag, producing the maddening symptom "the app says I have the thing AND keeps asking me to get it". The flag is a statement of intent, not a receipt of completion — set it when the user expresses the intent, and let the work be resumable/toppable behind it (which imgSync already made true here). Corollary spotted in the same read: any dedup/skip check must consult the durable store (or warm from it), not just the in-memory mirror that only exists when a flag was already on.

## v2.6.8 learning: a count-assert can be tripped by your OWN replacement text — the safety net works both ways

The batch patch asserted 'exactly 2 remaining bare downloadImages(names); calls' AFTER applying earlier edits — but one of those earlier edits' NEW text itself ended in that exact bare line, making the count 4 and aborting before the write. The assert did precisely its job (zero partial state), and the lesson is about authoring: when counting occurrences of an anchor string mid-script, remember that replacement texts you've already queued may add or remove instances of that same anchor. Unique per-site anchors avoid the interaction entirely.

## v2.6.9 learning: adding a new caller to an un-guarded async initializer is what turns "it never overlapped before" into a race

warmImgCache ran exactly once per session for years (startup OR toggle-on, mutually exclusive in practice), so it never needed a re-entry guard. The v2.6.8 fix added a third call site (downloadImages' pre-warm) reachable within the same seconds as the startup call — and the guard-shaped hole became a real double-cursor path leaking one blob-URL per image. Promise-memoization (`if(_warmP) return _warmP;`) is the canonical two-line shape: every caller shares the in-flight run, and completion state persists. Remember its lifecycle partner: any operation that INVALIDATES the warmed state (here imgClearAll emptying the memory map) must reset the memo, or the next legitimate warm returns a stale resolved promise and silently does nothing.

## v2.6.9 learning: when a Q&A answer leans on a mechanism ("X tops it up"), verify the mechanism's GATE before shipping the claim

The v2.6.8 reply told Johan imgSync would top up a partial cache — true only when conv.imgCache is already on, because imgSyncCheck's first line gates on it, which is precisely false in the stranded state under discussion. The code fix was right; the explanatory claim overreached by one unchecked conditional. Reading one line (the gate) before writing one sentence (the claim) is cheap insurance.

## v2.6.10 learning: a memory keyed on "the current setting" must be invalidated when that setting changes — fmt-relative Sets inverted their meaning on a mid-session format switch

localImgWrongFmt doesn't store "this card is a .jpg" (absolute); it stores "the PREFERRED extension is absent" (relative to conv.imgFmt at tag time). Every read re-interprets it against the CURRENT conv.imgFmt, so a settings switch silently inverts every existing tag — and the follow-on error path then mis-stamps the card as wholly missing. Any cache whose entries are interpreted relative to a mutable setting needs a clear (or a re-key) wired into that setting's change handler. The toggle-on clear already existed for the same reason; the format select was the forgotten sibling.

## v2.6.10 learning: promise-memoization needs a failure policy, not just a re-entry guard

The v2.6.9 memo solved the double-run race but memoized ALL outcomes — including "warmed zero entries" (transient DB error or an empty store), which pins a useless resolved promise forever and turns every later legitimate warm into a silent no-op. The cheap rule: memoize success, release on empty/failure (when retrying is cheap and the failure may be transient). `_warmP = inner().then(n => { if(!n) _warmP = null; return n; })` is the whole shape.

## v2.6.11 learning: a dispatch suite that drives the server directly can mask a missing CLIENT surface — feature-completeness needs one end-to-end trace per feature

The admin feature was "fully tested": dispatch test 14 exercised hello{admin}, the policy gate, and the 15-gate inheritance — by injecting the verb straight into handle(). Nothing ever asked "which client control produces this message?", and the answer was NONE: the standard client had no admin field, making the entire server feature unreachable in practice. The server-side suite proved the server; only a user-journey trace (button → payload → server branch) proves the FEATURE. Cheap rule: for every new verb, grep the client for its send site as part of the delivery gate.

## v2.6.11 learning: cleanup that lives only inside a debounced/scheduled path leaks on quiet systems

LOBBY_CONNS' self-prune ran inside scheduleRoomList's 300ms timer — which only fires when room events schedule it. The implicit assumption "cleanup happens regularly" was really "cleanup happens when the system is BUSY"; a quiet server (many browsers, few room events) never pruned. Lifecycle cleanup belongs at the lifecycle event itself (close), with scheduled prunes as redundancy — not the other way around.

## srv-2.6.9 learning: graceful-shutdown handlers written during development listen for the DEVELOPER's signal, not the DEPLOYMENT's

SIGINT is what a terminal Ctrl+C sends — the only stop signal a developer ever uses locally — so that's what got the flush handler. SIGTERM is what every process manager sends (systemd stop, docker stop, plain kill), i.e. the only stop signal an always-on deployment ever uses — and it was unhandled, silently downgrading every service-managed stop to a crash (≤60s state loss). When a project graduates from 'runs in my terminal' to 'runs as a service', re-check every process.on: the signal set that mattered changes underneath the same code.

## v2.6.12 learning: "the tutorial is outdated" splits into WRONG vs INCOMPLETE — and the fix differs completely

Reading the actual tutorial text before agreeing revealed it taught nothing false: the create/join flow it walks through is unchanged (the lobby is additive), and it even already said 'one server can host several rooms'. The gap was four missing NEW affordances. Incomplete ⇒ surgical additions in house style; wrong would have meant rewriting flow steps. Diagnosing which one it is BEFORE patching decided the entire shape of the work — and killed the perceived need for a server feature ('single-room mode') whose real purpose would have been keeping a text true.

## v2.6.12 learning: when a proposed client option would set SERVER policy, the authority model is the tiebreaker

'Choose Lobby vs single Room at create time' sounds like UX, but create is a CLIENT verb any guest can send — the option would let any room-creator lock a shared server's policy. Server-wide policy belongs to the machine's owner via CLI flags, and the wanted behaviour already existed there (`--create-policy admin`). Before adding a client control, ask whose decision it encodes; if the answer is 'the host machine's', it's a flag, not a checkbox.

## v2.6.13 learning: batch-patch anchors must match the ORIGINAL file, never the output of an earlier rep in the same batch

Second time this session (first: the bare downloadImages line in v2.6.8): an insert anchored on `name:'Play online — Host'` — text that only exists AFTER the rename-rep runs — but every rep's count-assert checks against s0, the untouched original. The assert aborted before any write, exactly as designed. Rule now written down where it belongs: when one edit's anchor depends on another edit's output, merge them into a single rep against the original text; a batch is not a sequence.

## v2.6.13 learning: macOS still ships bash 3.2 — `"${ARR[@]}"` on an EMPTY array aborts under set -u there, and a newer dev-container bash will hide it

The guided launcher built its flag list in an array; with every question skipped the array is empty, and bash 3.2 treats the empty-array expansion as an unbound variable under set -u — instant abort on the very platform (.command double-click) the script targets. The container's modern bash ran the dry-test green. The `${ARR[@]+"${ARR[@]}"}` form is the canonical 3.2-safe expansion. General rule: any shell script shipped to Mac users must be mentally linted against bash 3.2, whatever the CI bash says.

## v2.6.14 learning: <img src> and fetch() have DIFFERENT file:// privileges — an asset strategy that works for images can silently not work for data

The local-folder tier worked on file:// for images because browsers allow <img src> against local relative paths. Extending the same folder to vtes.json required fetch() — which browsers BLOCK against file:// (origin null). Same folder, same philosophy, different transport, different privilege. The honest resolution: ship the feature for the server/localhost/tunnel modes where fetch works, document the file:// limit right in the Settings copy (so nobody drops the file beside a double-clicked client and wonders), and note that the IndexedDB-cached copy already covers the file:// user. Rule: before promising 'the same folder works for X too', check X's transport — the folder is shared, the browser privileges are not.

## v2.6.14 learning: widening a security regex vs adding an exact-name whitelist branch — prefer the branch

vtes.json could have been allowed by adding `|json` to the /images/ extension regex — but that admits EVERY [a-z0-9-]+.json name forever. An explicit `if(file === 'vtes.json')` branch before the regex admits exactly one string, keeps the regex's guarantees untouched, and reads as intent. When the new need is ONE known filename, an equality check beats a grammar change.

## v2.6.15 learning: the file PICKER is the transport file:// always allows — the once-and-done pattern (load + cache on one click) turns it from a workaround into a feature

fetch() is blocked on file://, so the local vtes.json tier could not help a first-time fully-offline double-clicked client — and a FIRST start has no IndexedDB copy to fall back on either, making the chain a complete dead end. <input type=file> + FileReader is user-initiated and therefore permitted everywhere. Pairing the read with cacheVtesJson() makes it a ONE-TIME action: the picked file both loads now and seeds the cache for every later start. Corollary UX rule: every dead-end error message should name the recovery control ('Settings → 📁 From file…') — the user standing at the dead end is exactly the one who needs the sign.

## bot-0.1.0 learning: `pkill -f` sees your OWN wrapper's command line — a cleanup that names its target pattern kills itself

`pkill -f "elysium-server.js 8199"` matched the `/bin/sh -c` wrapper CARRYING that very string and killed the whole command (returncode −1, nothing after it ran — including the patch it preceded). The bracket trick makes the pattern non-self-matching: `pkill -f "elysium-server\.js [8]199"` — the target's cmdline contains `8199` (which regex `[8]199` matches) while ours contains the literal `[8]199` (which it does not). Same trap in `pgrep -af` diagnostics. Alternatives: kill by port owner, or exclude your own pid. Corollary from the same minutes: a suite that spawns a server should use a RANDOM port + room name per run, so an aborted run's straggler can never answer the next run with stale state.

## bot-0.1.0 learning: an ordered-consumption waitFor silently skips a companion message that arrived BEFORE the line you matched

The bot pushes its `board` BEFORE it chats the ack (wire-order is an implementation detail), but the test's `waitFor` advances a cursor past every examined message — so waiting for the ack CONSUMED the push, and the following "pool push matches" wait could never see it again. Fix class: pair every ordered-walk helper with a cursor-LESS whole-inbox variant (`waitAny`) and choose per assertion — ordered when sequencing IS the assertion, whole-inbox when the companion's relative order is not.

## bot-0.1.0 learning: a third-party client's `v` is a WIRE version, not its artifact version

`verMM` compares major.minor on every join; a bot that sends its own `0.1.0` greets every table with '⚠ Version mismatch'. The bot carries `BOT_VERSION` for itself and rides `WIRE_V '2.6.0'` in `create`/`join`. Generalizes protocol §2 to non-browser clients: anything that joins must speak the FAMILY's major.minor in `v`, whatever it calls itself. (Sibling detail from the same build: the ask-line must literally contain the token the answer grammar keys on — "Block?" belongs in the announce, not only in the docs.)


## v2.6.16 learning: the fx `verb` field is 40 chars of FREE TEXT — a ready-made side-channel for amounts in clones

The lock-clone caption renders `esc(opts.verb)` verbatim and the server relays `String(m.verb).slice(0,40)` untouched. So "bleeds" → "bleeds for 3" put the bleed amount in every remote clone with ZERO fx-protocol changes — no new field, no server bump for that half of the feature. Before inventing a new wire field for a small payload, check whether an existing free-text field already travels the exact path you need. (Corollary: the 40-char cap is now load-bearing — any future verb string must stay under it.)

## v2.6.16 learning: adding a wire verb is a SIX-file chain — treat it as one atomic checklist

`tally` touched: client (`MP_HANDLERS` + send sites), server (handler + room state + joinReply replay + start-clear), test-client-logic (`eq(keys.length, N)`), test-server-dispatch (count + a behaviour test), `check-versions.js` (BOTH hard-coded expected counts), and `ELYSIUM-PROTOCOL.md` (header note, c2s index, s2c index, §7 row, §8 row — the field cells must equal exactly what the live handlers read; the lint diffs them). Miss any one and a gate goes red; the fastest path is to write all six in the same pass, then run the gate battery once.


## v2.6.17 learning: a sender-side hook is INVISIBLE to remote clients — audit batch-affecting signals in BOTH endpoints

`saySend()` closed the card-play batch on 'It resolves', but the say RECEIVER (`MP_HANDLERS.say`) only called `showSay()` — so the verbal resolve never closed anyone else's batch, despite the help text promising it. The pattern generalizes: any behaviour attached where a message is SENT must be re-attached (or shared) where it is RECEIVED, or online play silently diverges from hotseat. When adding a semantic side-effect to a phrase/verb, grep both the send site and the MP_HANDLERS entry before calling it done.


## v2.6.18 learning: a `//` comment inside a replacement string EATS the rest of a ONE-LINE function

`hidePlayedSoon` is a single-line function. The patch replaced its opening (`… if(playedPinned) return;`) with `… if(avr.mode) return;   // comment` — and the untouched tail of the ORIGINAL line (clearTimeout … including the closing `}`) landed after the `//`, silently commented out. Result: unterminated function, `Unexpected end of input` 4000 lines later, and the harness pointing nowhere useful. Rules: (1) when the anchor sits mid-line, end the replacement with a `/* block comment */`, never `//`; (2) after any syntax failure, extract the `<script>` body and `node --check` it — that names a line; (3) diffing against the last gate-green delivery isolates the broken hunk in seconds when a homemade brace-counter chokes on regex literals.

## v2.6.18 learning: protocol section HEADINGS carry handler counts the lint never checks

`## 7. … verbs (51 seated …)` and `## 8. … messages (46)` sailed through the v2.6.16 tally pass untouched — test-protocol-doc lints the index blocks and field tables, not the prose counts in the headings. The six-file verb chain is therefore SEVEN entries: the two heading counts belong on the checklist next to check-versions' hard-coded pair.


## v2.6.20 learning: card ids are per-client sequential -- ownership/identity checks must be SEAT-scoped, never bare id lookups

`id = 'c' + (++state.seq)` means every client mints c1, c2, c3… -- the opponent's c12 and YOUR c12 are different cards with the same name. Any cross-seat feature that resolves a cid (the duel view, targets, give/attach) must qualify it with a seat first (`seat === mySeat() ? state.cards : net.boards[seat].pub`), exactly like the pub `target` field already does ({seat, cid} pairs). A bare `state.cards.get(foreignCid)` doesn't fail loudly -- it silently returns the WRONG card, with full local affordances attached.


## v2.6.26 learning: the tutorial engine DOCUMENTS its step schema in a header comment -- read it before writing steps

`advance:{on:'manual'|'click'|'event'|'predicate', name?, test?, hint?}` sits in a comment right above TUT_SECTIONS (~line 13478), and 'predicate - test() polls true on the reposition loop' is spelled out two lines later. The v2.6.25 section guessed `check:` for the predicate field from the shape of OTHER advance objects -- four steps would have stalled forever (tut.pred stays null, no crash, no error). The pre-test audit caught it by grepping an EXISTING `on:'predicate'` step. Generalises the read-before-write rule: when a subsystem has a schema comment, that comment IS the anchor to read first -- example steps second, guessing never.


## cardfx-v1 learning: KRCG card_text is a structured format in disguise — but "As above" starves a naive extractor's superior modes

372 library cards write their superior line as "As above, but …" — a per-segment pattern pass tags the inferior mode and leaves [DOM]/[OBF] EMPTY (Deflection's superior bounce simply vanishes). The compile-time fix: inherit the nearest earlier fx-bearing segment (prefer the same trigram), then let the segment's OWN extraction override ("but for +2 stealth" → 2). Two sibling structure facts from the same build: bracket tokens appear MID-line (~126 lines) so segmentation must split at token boundaries, and the lookahead split strands consecutive tokens ("[obf] " | "[ACTION MODIFIER] …") — carry a token-only chunk's tokens into the next chunk or the discipline requirement silently drops (Swallowed by the Night lost its [obf] before the fix; the gate now pins it).

## cardfx-v1 learning: in a derived-facts database, a WRONG tag beats a missing tag as the failure to fear — conservatism + provenance is the quality model

A bot that misses a tag falls back to defaults; a bot fed a wrong tag confidently misplays. So extraction patterns require the DIRECTED shapes ("burn N pool **from your prey**", "**they burn** N pool") and self-costs ("burn 1 pool to …") never read as threats — the gate asserts both directions (Emergency Preparations/Aversion NO, Enticement YES). Every entry carries `src:'auto'|'hand'` as the trust dial, and the curated tier REPLACES whole entries (no deep merge — predictable precedence). Same family: 77 real alias collisions (ADV twins, multi-group reprints) are DATA, not bugs — resolve with a deterministic preference ladder (non-ADV, then newest group) and report the count, never first-writer-wins silently.

## cardfx-v1 learning: unicode_escape over a string that already holds real UTF-8 text is a mojibake machine

Patch text mixing `\uXXXX` escapes with directly-typed em-dashes went through `.encode().decode('unicode_escape')` — the escapes resolved, but the REAL multibyte chars round-tripped as latin-1 (`—` → `â\x80\x94`) and landed corrupted in the doc header (caught by a `grep "â\|Ã"` sweep right after the write). Rule: in a UTF-8 Python heredoc, type the real characters directly and never run escape-decoding over the whole string; if escapes are unavoidable, the string must be pure ASCII first. Add the mojibake grep to the post-patch checklist for any doc edit that carries typography.


## cardfx-v1.1 learning: a data-format version question is a data-quality audit in disguise — and the client's parser is the contract to mirror, not re-derive

Johan's "is my file V3 or V4?" resolved to: the file is fine (static.krcg.org still ships v3), but chasing it surfaced (a) the v5 field renames hit exactly the fields cardfx needs (card_text→text, disciplines→discipline_requirement), and (b) a LIVE v3 quirk already in the current file — 'FLIGHT' as an uppercase full-name discipline on 9 library cards, which the compiler was passing through as a second vocabulary next to trigrams. The fix pattern: the compiler's normalizeCard() MIRRORS the client's parseV3Card/parseV5Card field map (verified at v2.5.87 against real v4-API samples) instead of inventing a parallel contract — one field map, two implementations in lockstep, same discipline as verMM. For the map's two UNKNOWNS (v5 cost shape, title), read defensively and COUNT in the report — degrade-and-count beats guess-and-mislabel, and it makes the first real-v5-file run self-auditing. Guard the catastrophic case in the CLI: zero fx-tagged cards = refuse to write, point at the format doc.


## Servern STÄNGER anslutningen över RATE_N — headless klienter behöver utbounds-pacing (12 juli 2026)

`elysium-server.js` svarar inte med drop på rate-limit (80 msg/10s per anslutning) utan med
`wsClose` — anslutningen dör. En bot i burst (paceMs 0: push+log+chat+say per aktör ≈ 20 msg/s)
åker ut mitt i sin tur och blir en död plats. **Regel: varje headless wire-klient ska dränera
sina sends genom en rullande-fönster-kö med marginal under serverns tak** (boten: tak 70/10s,
30ms inter-frame-gap, 250ms backoff). Detta är produktionsbeteende, inte testanpassning —
symptomet i testet var bara först synligt där ("[abuse] rate limit hit" i serverloggen är
signaturen).

## Cursor-baserad waitFor: vänta i KAUSAL ankomstordning (12 juli 2026)

Svitens `waitFor` konsumerar inkorgen framåt via cursor. När ett händelsepar anländer i ordningen
`turn-broadcast → bot-chat-not` (noten TRIGGAS av turnen) och testet väntar på noten först, har
cursorn passerat turn-meddelandet — nästa `waitFor(turn)` timar ut fast meddelandet ligger i
inkorgen. **Vänta alltid i den ordning meddelandena kausalt anländer** (orsak före verkan), eller
använd `waitAny` (helskanning) för det tidigare meddelandet. Besläktad fälla: absoluta
tillståndsasserts (pool==25) faller när tidigare sektioner ackumulerat tillstånd (influence
spenderar pool) — resolutions-asserts ska vara RELATIVA (regex-capture av ackens värde).


## Timer-debounce omordnar wiren — kö-koalescera i stället (12 juli 2026)

En timer-debouncad `push()` (skicka board 40ms senare) släppte chat-meddelanden FÖRE brädet de
kausalt följde — nedströms cursor-baserade konsumenter (svitens waitFor, potentiellt riktiga
klienter) föll i ordningsfällor. **Regel: fördröj aldrig enskilda meddelandetyper med timers i
en ordningskänslig ström. Koalescera i sändkön i stället:** en ordningsbevarande platshållare
(`{__board:true}`) som materialiserar FÄRSKASTE state vid drain-tillfället — burstar kollapsar
till ett wire-meddelande, kausal ordning håller, och innehållet är alltid nyast.

## Flaky failure-punkt som VANDRAR = mättnad, inte logikfel (12 juli 2026)

När en svit faller på OLIKA asserts varje körning efter en ändring som ökar meddelandevolymen:
misstänk resurskö-mättnad (här: botens pacer-fönster 70/10s fyllt av v0.3:s kortspel+draws →
kaskadande 250ms-backoffs → timeouts varhelst kön råkade vara djupast). Diagnos: aktivera den
tystade loggen (fel i `.catch(e => o.log(...))` är osynliga när o.log är noop i testet!) och
räkna sändvolym per fönster. Fix på volymsidan (koalescering) + spridning (paceMs), inte högre
timeouts.


## __dirname-förankrad persistens besegrar cwd-isolering — testa mot en KOPIA (12 juli 2026)

Serverns store är `path.resolve(__dirname, 'elysium-rooms.json')` med snapshot var 60:e sekund —
så en testsvit som isolerar via färsk mkdtemp-CWD skriver ÄNDÅ till den riktiga filen. Symptomet
kom först efter en hel dags körningar: exakt vid MAX_ROOMS=50 började varje `create` nekas
("The server is full") och sviten gick 0/1 tvärt, på ren processtabell, utan kodändring.
**Regler:** (1) tester som spawnar en process med egen persistens ska spawna en KOPIA av skriptet
inne i tmp-katalogen (⇒ __dirname = tmp), inte originalet med ändrad cwd; (2) diagnossignaturen
"svit som varit grön hela dagen börjar plötsligt falla på första create/join" ⇒ kolla
kapacitetstak mot ackumulerad persistens INNAN logikjakt; (3) cross-turn-greppar över
beteendeloggar fejkar "dubbletter" — samma aktör i nästa tur är laglig; filtrera per tur innan
slutsats.


## Väntor måste knytas till LIVHET — och tracelagret betalade sig dag ett (12 juli 2026)

Botens Block?-fönster väntade askSecs på svar från en prey som var OUSTAD — som aldrig armar
(out-guarden) och aldrig säger Pass. I slutspel med många aktörer blev det askSecs × N av död
tid, nog för att trippa wall-timeouts. **Regel: varje vänta-på-motpart ska (a) kolla motpartens
livhet vid ÖPPNING och (b) prenumerera på livhetsförändringen (roster-hook) mitt-i.** Diagnosen
kom via arenans JSONL-traces + en frysfångare som dumpade varje bots inre (ask/pending/kö/timer-
forensik med _destroyed/_called) — två falska spår (köstall, "meddelandestorm" som var friskt
spel) föll på DATA i stället för teori. Bygg observationsverktyget FÖRE jakten: tracelagret
designades för persona-utvärdering och löste sin första bugg samma dag.


## B1-falsk-pass, token bucket och skuggade handlers — tre snabba (12 juli 2026)

**(1) Bygg till scratch och cmp:a — och verifiera att kedjans kataloger är SAMMA.**
`split_client.py` skriver fragment till `/home/claude/elysium-src`; `elysium-build.js` läser
`ROOT/elysium-src`. Med en stale fragmentkatalog gav default-bygget en byte-identisk FALSK
PASS mot för-redigeringsinnehåll. Recept: kopiera källan till /tmp/original.html → split →
synka fragmentkatalogen → bygg till /tmp/rebuilt.html → `cmp original rebuilt`. Aldrig
default-overwrite som verifiering.

**(2) Token bucket slår rullande-fönster-cap för utgående pacing.** Fönster-cap (≤70/10s)
låter två snabba turer FYLLA fönstret och stallar sedan nästa kritiska meddelande i sekunder
(pending-maskinens Pass satt fast bakom 250ms-backoffs — instrumentera pacern och LETA
'backoff vid kritisk send' innan logikjakt). En bucket (burst 8, påfyllnad 1/140ms) ger samma
budget med BEGRÄNSAD värsta-latens per meddelande.

**(3) Dubbla nycklar i objektliteraler skuggar tyst — SENARE vinner.** En ny handler i en
handler-tabell måste föregås av `grep verbnamn` i filen: v0.1 hade redan `forceSetPool`, min
nya definition högre upp var död kod och testet jagade fel frastext. Symptom: "meddelandet
anländer (onEvent ser det) men 'min' handler tiger".


## Stora spann patchas med index-kirurgi mot filens egna bytes (12 juli 2026)

Två ankarrekonstruktioner av showSay-kroppen föll på osynliga byte-skillnader (escape-lager +
kommentarslydelser) trots repr-läsning. Receptet som håller för FLYTT/OMSLUTNING av stora
kodspann: (1) välj KORTA unika markörer för start och slut; (2) slut-markören behöver bara
vara först-efter-start (globala unikhetskrav på vanliga rader som `host.appendChild(d);`
fäller patchen i onödan) — men sätt en maxspann-vakt; (3) SKIVA innehållet ur filen
(`s[i:j+len(b)]`) och återanvänd de bytesen i den nya konstruktionen i stället för att skriva
om dem. Rekonstruktion är för sträng-LIKA ersättningar; kirurgi är för strukturflyttar.


## Rekognoscera med användarens vokabulär och UI-strängarna — inte begreppssynonymer (12 juli 2026)

Johans "stoppur" fanns redan: **Reaction timer** (rumsfältet `#mpReact` 3–30 s default 5,
⏱-knappen `#btnDecide`, wire-verbet `decide` som redan bar `who`). Min recon greppade "clock/
timer/stopwatch" som KONCEPT och hittade bara matchklockan — så jag byggde en dubblett-chip,
en dubblett-⏱-knapp och en påhittad fryst lograd, bredvid originalet. **Regler:** (1) greppa
knapptitlar/tooltips/labels (`title=`, `<label>`) — features heter det UI:t kallar dem, inte
det jag kallar dem; (2) när användaren säger "vi hade ju redan X" är det ett STOPP-kommando:
re-rekognoscera innan design; (3) en verb-grep i servern (`grep "  verbname(conn"`-mönstret
över hela handler-tabellen) hade listat `decide` direkt — inventera handler-tabellen när en
"ny" mekanism övervägs.


## Verifiera regeltext mot källa, inte minne — särskilt när symmetrin ser för enkel ut (13 juli 2026)

Jag implementerade Deflection som "omdirigera till AKTÖRENS prey" ur minnet — lät rimligt,
kompilerade, gick igenom node --check. Den riktiga korttexten säger "till en ANNAN
METHUSELAH ÄN AKTÖRENS KONTROLLANT" (försvararens fria val, konventionellt sitt EGET prey).
Symptomet som borde ha väckt misstanke tidigare: mitt facit degenererade till "studsar
tillbaka på aktören" i ett 2-spelartest — när en regel-implementation kollapsar till att
motsäga sitt eget syfte i det ENKLASTE testfallet, är det en signal att verifiera källan,
inte att komplicera testet för att dölja symtomet. Regel: för VARJE korttext-baserad
mekanik (målval, kostnad, villkor) — sök upp den FAKTISKA lydelsen (vekn.net, Black
Chantry-klargöranden) innan kodning, inte efter ett test råkar avslöja något konstigt.

## Cursor-baserad waitFor: skriv testets väntor i SÄNDNINGSORDNING, inte önskad läsordning (13 juli 2026)

Andra gången detta mönster bet — nu i mitt EGET nya test. `_commitBlock` skickar 'Block!'
(rad 1) FÖRE wake-annonsen (senare rad), men testet väntade på wake FÖRST sedan 'Block!' —
cursorn skenar förbi det tidigare meddelandet medan den skannar efter det som efterfrågas
FÖRST i koden, och kan aldrig gå bakåt. Regel: innan du skriver flera sekventiella waitFor
mot samma klient, lista ut den FAKTISKA sändningsordningen ur källkoden FÖRST — gissa
aldrig utifrån vad som känns naturligt att kolla i.


## Ett rimligt regelantagande kan ändå vara farligt om exekveringen inte kollar sitt eget facit (13 juli 2026)

Deflection-fixen (v0.4.1) avslöjade ett mönster värt att bära vidare: jag hade redan
KORRIGERAT bounce-målet en gång (aktören → eget prey) och trodde saken klar. Men jag
verifierade aldrig det TRIVIALA gränsfallet (2 spelare) mot den nya koden — Johan gjorde
det åt mig, som en lekmannaobservation, inte en buggrapport. Regel: när en regelkorrigering
gäller MÅLVAL (vem/vad ett effekt pekar på), testa alltid det MINSTA möjliga bordet (2
spelare) som ett explicit gränsfall — målval-logik som ser rimlig ut vid 3+ spelare kollapsar
ofta tyst vid 2, eftersom "min granne" och "din granne" blir samma person.

## Beslut och exekvering måste läsa samma facit (13 juli 2026)

`interceptPotential()` (beslutet) och `_bestInterceptFor` (exekveringen) användes båda för
"hur mycket intercept har jag" — men bara EN av dem kollade den gång-per-aktion-ledger som
faktiskt gäller. Två system som svarar på samma fråga MÅSTE läsa samma tillstånd, annars
uppstår en tyst drift där beslutet lovar något exekveringen inte kan hålla (här: ett
"nakent" blockförsök utan kort, som aldrig får sin verdikt). Regel: när en gate/ledger/
begränsning läggs till, sök upp ALLA ställen som frågar samma sak och verifiera att de
delar exakt samma kontrollerade tillstånd — inte bara den plats buggen först visade sig.


## Kodkommentarer är inte dokumentation — journalposten ÄR ritualen (13 juli 2026)

v0.4.2 skeppades med fem korrekta fixar och utmärkta kodkommentarer — men NOLL
dokumentsvep: ingen journalpost, spec-tabellen kvar på 0.4.1, CLAUDE/context orörda.
Nästa session (eller nästa granskningsfråga) möter då en kod som är NYARE än sin egen
dokumentation och måste arkeologera fram vad som hänt ur kommentarer — exakt det läge
levande-dokument-ritualen finns för att förhindra. Regel: versionsbumpen och journalposten
är EN odelbar handling; en bump utan post är ett ritualbrott oavsett hur bra
kodkommentarerna är. (Upptäckt av att koden sa 0.4.2 medan mitt eget minne och alla
dokument sa 0.4.1 — filerna på disk vann, som de ska.)

## Regelboks-bokföring (lås, kostnader) granskas separat från lyckliga-vägen-logik (13 juli 2026)

M2:s combat fungerade perfekt i alla tester — och ändå stred blockeraren GRATIS: succé-
vägen glömde regelbokens "the blocking minion locks". Testerna asserterade skada, torpor
och §12-flöden men ingen fråga om vad blocket KOSTAR. Regel: för varje regelboks-verb
(block, wake, bounce, strike) — lista dess BOKFÖRING (lås? blod? kort? Edge?) som en egen
kolumn och assertera den separat från utfallet; lyckliga vägen döljer gratis-resurser
tyst.

## Ett "read-only" system kan vara en outnyttjad generisk mekanism, inte ett nytt behov (13 juli 2026)

Johan ville att bottens kort skulle bli manipulerbara av alla — lät som ett nytt
behörighetssystem. Men motståndarkorts-menyn hade redan ett generiskt `ctrl`-verb
(blood/blue/green/lock/flip) från cross-board-give-arbetet (v2.5.20–26), bara gatat på
`owner===net.you` i stället för på SÄTET. Att byta ett namngivet-ägare-villkor mot ett
namngivet-säte-villkor (`_mine || _botSeat`) är en ren utvidgning av en befintlig
mekanism, inte ett nytt system — värt att alltid fråga "finns redan en generisk switch
här som bara är för snävt gatad?" innan man designar från scratch.

**Bieffekt av att äntligen öva den vägen mot en ny mottagartyp:** `elysium-bot.js` hade
NOLL `ctrl`-hantering — mekanismen hade bara någonsin körts mot riktiga människo-klienter
(som har en egen holder-mottagare vid `owner===m.from`-kollen), aldrig mot en headless
bot, eftersom den gamla owner-gaten aldrig visade knapparna mot ett bot-säte över huvud
taget. En väl beprövad mekanism kan alltså ha en HELT otestad gren bara för att den
aldrig fått rätt sorts mottagare att träffa. Regel: när en ny "vem får nå detta"-regel
öppnar en gammal mekanism mot en ny mottagartyp, verifiera att mottagaren faktiskt HAR
en implementation för den — anta inte att "mekanismen finns redan" betyder "alla sidor
av den är byggda".

**Zon-flytt via befintlig `move()` i stället för handrullad zon-bokföring:** för den
riktiga människo-holder-mottagaren (kort du kontrollerar men som ligger hos någon annan)
används `move(c,'torpor')`/`move(c,'ready')` i stället för att sätta `c.zone` direkt —
kortet är en genuin lokal `state.cards`-post (skapad via `makeCard` i `given`-hanteraren,
zon-registrerad precis som ett eget kort), så `move()` sköter zon-array-bokföringen,
layout och rise/flip-fx gratis. Den bara-pub-objekt-baserade vägen (hotseat-apply +
online-optimism, `ctrlApply`) sätter `k.zone` direkt eftersom den aldrig har en riktig
`state.cards`-post att köra `move()` på.

## Vy-läges-syskondrift: en fix till L3/L4 som aldrig speglades till L2 (13 juli 2026)

v2.5.76 fixade korrekt att L3/L4:s bottendock ("bottenpeek") skulle respektera
`conv.dockDrag`/`dockPinned` istället för att stänga sig blint när ett hand-/hög-kort
drogs ut — med en tydlig kod-kommentar om att L2 hade "den sköna sibling-fixen" i
biblioteks/crypt-spökdraget. Men handkortens EGNA l2cols-gren (samma fil, samma
drag-hanterare, bara ett annat `else if`-block några rader längre ner) fick aldrig
samma behandling — den stängde dockan ovillkorligt vid varje dragstart, oavsett
inställning eller nål. Samma klass av bugg som "L4 dispatch chain drift" i
protokollagret, fast i UI-lagret: när en fix landar för ETT vy-läge (L3/L4), sök
grep efter systervillkoren för de ANDRA vy-lägena (L2 cols, L2 Home) i SAMMA
funktion/hanterare och verifiera att de fick samma fix — en kodkommentar som säger
"nu gör X detsamma som Y" är ett löfte, inte ett bevis, om ingen faktiskt grep:ade
efter alla ställen X och Y förekommer.
